Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Mia. Mia had a brother named Liam. One day, Liam got a pretty dress as a present.

Mia felt jealous. "Why did Liam get something and I didn't?" she thought. Mia got so angry that she took the pretty dress and hid it!

Liam couldn't find his new thing and started to cry. Mom asked, "Mia, do you know where it is?"

Mia felt bad seeing Liam so sad. She went and got the pretty dress and said, "I'm sorry. I took it because I was jealous."

Mom explained, "Everyone gets different things at different times. Liam's special day will be your special day another time." Mia hugged Liam and learned that jealousy only makes everyone sad.



Once upon a time, a little boy named Charlie and a little boy named Jack were playing together. They both wanted to use the ball.

"Me first!" yelled Charlie. "No, me first!" yelled Jack. They pushed and pulled, and soon they were both very upset.

An older kid saw them fighting and came over. "Why don't you take turns? One person goes, then the other person goes."

Charlie went first for a little while, then it was Jack's turn. They kept switching, and guess what? They both got to play!

Charlie and Jack learned that taking turns is fair. Everyone gets a chance, and no one feels left out. Now they always take turns and never fight!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Bella. Bella was very excited about to go to the park. But her mommy said she had to wait.

"I don't want to wait! I want it now!" said Bella. She started to stomp her feet and whine.

But being impatient didn't help. It just made Bella feel worse. her mommy said, "Being upset won't make time go faster."

Bella tried to be patient. She played with toys and helped her mommy. Before Bella knew it, it was time!

"Waiting wasn't so bad!" said Bella with a big smile. She learned that being patient and finding fun things to do makes waiting easier. Good things come to those who wait!



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Henry. Henry was afraid of water. Whenever he saw water, he would hide!

One day, his dad said, "Let's try to be brave together." Henry was nervous but held his dad's hand tight.

They faced water slowly and carefully. At first, Henry was still scared. But his dad was right there.

Little by little, Henry felt less afraid. He realized that with help, water wasn't so scary after all!

Henry was so proud of being brave! He learned that it's okay to be afraid, but facing your fears makes you stronger. And having someone to help makes it easier.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Jasper. One day at the playground, Jasper saw a new little girl named Lydia.

At first, Jasper was too shy to say hello. What if the new kid didn't like him? Jasper just watched from far away.

But then Jasper thought, "Maybe Lydia wants a friend too!" So Jasper walked over and said, "Hi! Want to play?"

Lydia's face lit up with a big smile. "Yes! I was hoping someone would ask!" They played together and had so much fun!

Jasper learned that being brave and saying hello can make new friends. Everyone wants to be included. Now Jasper and Lydia are best friends!



Once upon a time, a caring little boy named Ryan went to the beach with his grandpa. Ryan loved to explore and discover new things.

While walking, Ryan saw a frozen lake. It looked exciting! He forgot what his grandpa said about staying close. Ryan ran toward it to take a closer look.

"Stop!" yelled his grandpa. But Ryan got too close and almost fell in! His grandpa grabbed him just in time.

Ryan's heart was beating fast. He was very scared. "Grandpa, I'm sorry," Ryan said with tears in his eyes.

His grandpa hugged Ryan tight. "I'm glad you're safe. Some places are dangerous, and that's why we must be careful." Ryan promised to always listen and never wander off again.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Hazel. Hazel was running in the house, even though her daddy said not to.

While playing, Hazel hurt their finger! It hurt a lot and Hazel started to cry. Her daddy came running to help.

Daddy cleaned the boo-boo and gave Hazel a bandage. "This is why I said to be careful," daddy explained gently.

Hazel felt better after a hug and a kiss. But she learned an important lesson: the rules are there to keep her safe.

From then on, Hazel remembered to be more careful. Getting hurt is no fun, and following the rules helps avoid accidents!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Emma. One day, her dad made delicious crackers for Emma and her little brother Ryan.

Dad put the crackers on the table. "Make sure you share nicely," said dad. But Emma wanted all the crackers for herself!

When Ryan wasn't looking, Emma took most of the crackers. She ate and ate until her tummy hurt very much!

Emma felt sick and couldn't play anymore. Ryan was sad because there wasn't enough crackers left. Dad came and saw what happened.

"Being greedy doesn't make you happy," said dad. "Now you don't feel good, and Ryan is sad." Emma said sorry to Ryan and learned that being greedy only makes everyone feel bad.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Jack. Jack didn't like to listen to rules. He thought rules were boring!

One day, Jack's mommy said not to do something. But Jack didn't listen. He kept touching the hot stove anyway.

Then something bad happened. Jack burned their hand and it hurt for a long time. He wished he had listened!

Jack's mommy wasn't angry, just sad. "I told you because I love you and want to keep you safe," mommy said.

Jack finally understood. Rules aren't to be mean—they're to protect us! He learned that lesson the hard way. Now he listens more carefully.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Leo. Leo only wanted to eat soda. "I don't like carrots!" he would say every day.

His daddy tried to give Leo healthy food, but Leo always said no. He only ate soda for days and days.

Soon, Leo didn't feel good. His tummy hurt and he had no energy to play. The doctor said Leo needed to eat healthy food to feel better.

Leo tried the carrots, just a tiny bite. Hey, it wasn't so bad! Actually, it was pretty good! He tried more healthy foods and started feeling much better.

Now Leo eats lots of good food that makes him strong. He still has treats sometimes, but he knows healthy food is important!



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Ben. One day, his dad made delicious fruit for Ben and his little sister Sara.

Dad put the fruit on the table. "Make sure you share nicely," said dad. But Ben wanted all the fruit for himself!

When Sara wasn't looking, Ben took most of the fruit. He ate and ate until his tummy hurt very much!

Ben felt sick and couldn't play anymore. Sara was sad because there wasn't enough fruit left. Dad came and saw what happened.

"Being greedy doesn't make you happy," said dad. "Now you don't feel good, and Sara is sad." Ben said sorry to Sara and learned that being greedy only makes everyone feel bad.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Cole who had a special blocks. It was his favorite toy in the whole world!

But Cole didn't take good care of it. He left it outside in the rain, threw it around, and never put it away nicely.

One day, the blocks broke! A piece fell off and it didn't work anymore. Cole was so sad and cried. He wanted his favorite toy back!

His mommy said, "If you had taken better care of it, it might not have broken. Things need love and care."

Cole learned to take care of his things. He puts toys away nicely now and treats them gently. Taking care of our things makes them last longer!



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Sam. Sam had a sister named Clara. One day, Clara got a pretty dress as a present.

Sam felt jealous. "Why did Clara get something and I didn't?" he thought. Sam got so angry that he took the pretty dress and hid it!

Clara couldn't find her new thing and started to cry. Mommy asked, "Sam, do you know where it is?"

Sam felt bad seeing Clara so sad. He went and got the pretty dress and said, "I'm sorry. I took it because I was jealous."

Mommy explained, "Everyone gets different things at different times. Clara's special day will be your special day another time." Sam hugged Clara and learned that jealousy only makes everyone sad.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Tommy who had a special doll. It was his favorite toy in the whole world!

But Tommy didn't take good care of it. He left it outside in the rain, threw it around, and never put it away nicely.

One day, the doll broke! A piece fell off and it didn't work anymore. Tommy was so sad and cried. He wanted his favorite toy back!

His mom said, "If you had taken better care of it, it might not have broken. Things need love and care."

Tommy learned to take care of his things. He puts toys away nicely now and treats them gently. Taking care of our things makes them last longer!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Bella. One day, Bella saw mom with the dishes. At first, Bella just wanted to keep playing.

But then Bella thought, "What if that was me? I would want someone to help!" So Bella went over and asked, "Can I help you?"

The person smiled big and said, "Yes, please! That's so kind of you!" Bella helped as best as she could.

When it was done, the person said, "Thank you so much! You are a wonderful helper!" Bella felt so happy inside, happier than when playing alone.

Her mom said, "I'm so proud of you for helping!" Bella learned that helping others makes everyone feel good, especially yourself.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Jake. At school, a bigger kid named Eli was mean to him. Eli called Jake names and made him feel sad.

Jake didn't want to go to school anymore. He would cry and feel scared. But he didn't tell anyone what was happening.

Finally, his dad noticed something was wrong. Jake told them about Eli. Together, they talked to the teacher.

The teacher helped stop the bullying. Eli learned that being mean is wrong. Jake learned that it's important to tell grown-ups when someone is being mean.

Jake felt safe again! He learned that telling someone isn't tattling—it's asking for help. We should always speak up when something is wrong!



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Leo. Every morning, Leo didn't want to get up. He played and dawdled instead of getting ready.

One day, because Leo was so slow, he missed the school bus! His mom had to drive him, and they were both late.

At school, Leo had missed story time, the best part of the day! He was so sad. His friends had all the fun without him.

That night, his mom helped make a list: wake up, brush teeth, get dressed, eat breakfast. Leo put stickers on the list when he finished each thing.

The next day, Leo got ready quickly! He caught the bus and didn't miss anything. Having a routine makes mornings easier and better!



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Luke. Luke had a favorite jump rope that he loved very much. He played with it every day.

One day, his little sister Pearl came and asked, "Can I play with your jump rope?" But Luke said, "No! It's mine! Go away!"

Pearl was very sad and started to cry. Luke kept playing alone, but it didn't feel fun anymore. He saw how sad Pearl was and felt bad inside.

Finally, Luke went to Pearl and said, "I'm sorry. We can play together." Pearl's face lit up with a big smile. They played with the jump rope together and had so much more fun!

Luke learned that sharing makes everyone happy. When we share, we make more friends and have more fun.



Once upon a time, a little boy named Leo went to the beach with his daddy. It was a hot day and the water looked so inviting!

His daddy said, "Wait for me before going in the water." But Leo was too excited. He ran and jumped right in!

The water was deeper than Leo thought! He couldn't touch the bottom and got scared. He started to splash and cry for help.

His daddy quickly jumped in and pulled Leo out. They were both very shaken up.

Leo learned an important lesson that day. Water can be dangerous! Always wait for a grown-up, and never swim alone. Now Leo always asks for permission before going near water.



Once upon a time, a little girl named Ella went to the playground with her grandma. They were having a nice day together.

While her grandma was looking at something, a stranger came up to Ella. The stranger smiled and said, "Would you like some candy? Come with me!"

Ella remembered what her grandma had taught her. She said loudly, "No! I don't talk to strangers!" Then Ella ran back to her grandma.

Ella told her grandma what happened. Grandma was so proud! "You did the right thing! Never go anywhere with someone you don't know."

Ella felt brave and safe. She learned that it's always okay to say no to strangers and run to a grown-up you trust.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Chloe. Chloe was always in a hurry. She never wanted to slow down!

One day, her dad said, "Be careful! Don't go so fast!" But Chloe didn't listen. She was riding a bike too fast, going faster and faster.

Suddenly, Chloe tripped and fell! She scraped her knee and it hurt a lot. Chloe started to cry.

Her dad came and put a bandage on the scrape. "This is why I asked you to slow down," said dad gently.

Chloe's knee hurt for several days. She learned that rushing can lead to accidents. It's better to slow down and be careful than to get hurt.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Chloe. One day, Chloe took their snack to her friend Ben. Ben was very sad.

At first, Chloe didn't want to say sorry. She felt embarrassed and a little stubborn. But Ben wouldn't play with her anymore.

Chloe's mom said, "When we hurt someone, we need to say sorry. It helps fix the hurt."

Chloe found Ben and said, "I'm really sorry for what I did. It was wrong. Can you forgive me?" Ben smiled and said yes.

They hugged and played together again! Chloe learned that saying sorry is hard but important. It makes friendships strong and helps everyone feel better.

Emma learned that promises are very important. When we break a promise, we hurt our friends. From then on, Emma always kept her promises.

Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Anna who had a brother named Jake. One day, they both wanted the TV remote.

"It's mine!" yelled Anna. "No, it's mine!" yelled Jake. They started pushing and grabbing. Soon they were really fighting!

Mom heard the noise and came in. "Stop!" said mom. "Fighting is not okay!" Both Anna and Jake were in trouble.

They had to sit in time-out and think about what they did. Mom said, "Use your words, not your hands. Talk about problems."

Anna and Jake said sorry to each other. They learned to take turns and talk instead of fight. Using words is much better than fighting!

Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Daisy. Daisy never liked to clean up. Her room was always very messy!

One day, Daisy couldn't find her lucky sock. She looked everywhere but there was so much stuff on the floor! Daisy started to cry.

Her dad said, "If you kept your room clean, you could find your things." Daisy knew dad was right.

Together, they cleaned the whole room. They picked up toys, folded clothes, and put things in their place. And guess what? They found the lucky sock!

Daisy was so happy! She learned that keeping things clean helps you find what you need. A tidy room is a happy room!

Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Clara. One day, Clara saw a bottle on the counter. It looked like candy!

Clara reached for it, but her mommy quickly took it away. "No! That's medicine, not candy!" said mommy.

"But it looks yummy," said Clara. Mommy sat down with Clara to explain something important.

"Medicine helps sick people feel better, but it can make healthy people very sick. Only grown-ups can give medicine, and only when someone needs it."

Clara understood now. Medicine is not a treat. She promised to never touch medicine bottles. Some things that look like candy can be dangerous!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Lily. One day, Lily heard some big kids say a word that sounded funny. So Lily said it too!

Her mommy's face looked very surprised and sad. "Where did you learn that word?" asked mommy. "That's a bad word that hurts people's feelings."

Lily didn't know! She just thought it sounded funny. But now she understood that some words can make people feel bad.

Mommy explained, "Kind words make people happy. Mean words make people sad. We always want to use kind words."

Lily felt sorry for saying the bad word. She learned to think before speaking. Now Lily uses kind words that make people smile!

Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Max. One day, Max really wanted to skip bath time. But his dad said no.

Max got very angry! He started to scream and cry and kick his feet. He threw a big tantrum right there!

But the tantrum didn't work. his dad waited until Max calmed down. "Screaming won't change my answer," said dad.

Max was tired from all the crying. He felt silly. The tantrum didn't get him what he wanted. It just made him tired and sad.

Max learned that throwing tantrums doesn't help. It's better to use words and accept when the answer is no. Sometimes grown-ups know what's best.

Once upon a time, a little boy named Zach went to the store with his daddy. There were so many exciting things to see!

Zach saw something shiny and colorful. Without thinking, he walked toward it, leaving his daddy behind. Zach walked and walked until...

He looked around and didn't see his daddy anywhere! Zach was lost! He felt very scared and started to cry.

A kind worker found Zach and helped find his daddy. When they were together again, Zach hugged his daddy so tight!

"Never wander off without me," said daddy. Zach learned to always stay close to his daddy in busy places. It's scary to be lost.

Once upon a time, a little girl named Luna wanted to make a sandcastle. She tried and tried, but it was too hard to do alone!

Then Luna's friend Chloe came by. "Need help?" asked Chloe. At first, Luna said, "No, I can do it myself!"

But after trying more and failing, Luna finally said, "Okay, please help me." Together, they started working.

With two people helping, the job became easy! They finished quickly and had so much fun doing it together. They high-fived and celebrated!

Luna learned that it's okay to ask for help. Working together makes hard things easier and more fun. Two friends are better than one!

One day, the puzzle broke! A piece fell off and it didn't work anymore. Ella was so sad and cried. She wanted her favorite toy back!

Her mommy said, "If you had taken better care of it, it might not have broken. Things need love and care."

Ella learned to take care of her things. She puts toys away nicely now and treats them gently. Taking care of our things makes them last longer!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Violet. At school, a bigger kid named Ivy was mean to her. Ivy called Violet names and made her feel sad.

Violet didn't want to go to school anymore. She would cry and feel scared. But she didn't tell anyone what was happening.

Finally, her mom noticed something was wrong. Violet told them about Ivy. Together, they talked to the teacher.

The teacher helped stop the bullying. Ivy learned that being mean is wrong. Violet learned that it's important to tell grown-ups when someone is being mean.

Violet felt safe again! She learned that telling someone isn't tattling—it's asking for help. We should always speak up when something is wrong!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Bella. Bella was afraid of loud noises. Whenever she saw loud noises, she would hide!

One day, her mom said, "Let's try to be brave together." Bella was nervous but held her mom's hand tight.

They faced loud noises slowly and carefully. At first, Bella was still scared. But her mom was right there.

Little by little, Bella felt less afraid. She realized that with help, loud noises wasn't so scary after all!

Bella was so proud of being brave! She learned that it's okay to be afraid, but facing your fears makes you stronger. And having someone to help makes it easier.



Once upon a time, a little boy named Eli went to the store with his dad. There were so many exciting things to see!

Eli saw something shiny and colorful. Without thinking, he walked toward it, leaving his dad behind. Eli walked and walked until...

He looked around and didn't see his dad anywhere! Eli was lost! He felt very scared and started to cry.

A kind worker found Eli and helped find his dad. When they were together again, Eli hugged his dad so tight!

"Never wander off without me," said dad. Eli learned to always stay close to his dad in busy places. It's scary to be lost.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Tim who had a special balloon. It was his favorite toy in the whole world!

But Tim didn't take good care of it. He left it outside in the rain, threw it around, and never put it away nicely.

One day, the balloon broke! A piece fell off and it didn't work anymore. Tim was so sad and cried. He wanted his favorite toy back!

His dad said, "If you had taken better care of it, it might not have broken. Things need love and care."

Tim learned to take care of his things. He puts toys away nicely now and treats them gently. Taking care of our things makes them last longer!



Once upon a time, a little boy named Jack went to the pond with his mommy. It was a hot day and the water looked so inviting!

His mommy said, "Wait for me before going in the water." But Jack was too excited. He ran and jumped right in!

The water was deeper than Jack thought! He couldn't touch the bottom and got scared. He started to splash and cry for help.

His mommy quickly jumped in and pulled Jack out. They were both very shaken up.

Jack learned an important lesson that day. Water can be dangerous! Always wait for a grown-up, and never swim alone. Now Jack always asks for permission before going near water.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Nora. Nora loved watching cartoons on the TV. She watched for hours and hours every day.

Her daddy said, "You watch too much TV. Go play outside!" But Nora didn't want to stop.

After many days of too much TV, Nora's head started to hurt. Her eyes felt tired. She didn't feel good at all.

The doctor said Nora needed to rest her eyes and play more. So Nora went outside and discovered how fun it was to run and play!

Nora learned that too much TV isn't good for you. Playing outside and using your imagination is much more fun. Now Nora only watches a little TV each day.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Hugo. Hugo had a friend named Eli. They promised to build a sandcastle the next day.

But when the next day came, Hugo decided to do something else instead. He forgot all about the promise to Eli.

Eli waited and waited, but Hugo never came. Eli felt very sad and disappointed. When Hugo saw Eli later, Eli was crying.

"You promised!" said Eli. Hugo suddenly remembered and felt terrible. "I'm so sorry," said Hugo. "I forgot."

Hugo learned that promises are very important. When we break a promise, we hurt our friends. From then on, Hugo always kept his promises.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Leah. One day, Leah really wanted another cookie. But her daddy said no.

Leah got very angry! She started to scream and cry and kick her feet. She threw a big tantrum right there!

But the tantrum didn't work. her daddy waited until Leah calmed down. "Screaming won't change my answer," said daddy.

Leah was tired from all the crying. She felt silly. The tantrum didn't get her what she wanted. It just made her tired and sad.

Leah learned that throwing tantrums doesn't help. It's better to use words and accept when the answer is no. Sometimes grown-ups know what's best.

Once upon a time, a brave little boy named Tim went to the beach with his dad. Tim loved to explore and discover new things.

While walking, Tim saw a steep cliff. It looked exciting! He forgot what his dad said about staying close. Tim ran toward it to take a closer look.

"Stop!" yelled his dad. But Tim got too close and almost fell in! His dad grabbed him just in time.

Tim's heart was beating fast. He was very scared. "Dad, I'm sorry," Tim said with tears in his eyes.

His dad hugged Tim tight. "I'm glad you're safe. Some places are dangerous, and that's why we must be careful." Tim promised to always listen and never wander off again.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Tim. Tim had a sister named Hazel. One day, Hazel got a pretty dress as a present.

Tim felt jealous. "Why did Hazel get something and I didn't?" he thought. Tim got so angry that he took the pretty dress and hid it!

Hazel couldn't find her new thing and started to cry. Daddy asked, "Tim, do you know where it is?"

Tim felt bad seeing Hazel so sad. He went and got the pretty dress and said, "I'm sorry. I took it because I was jealous."

Daddy explained, "Everyone gets different things at different times. Hazel's special day will be your special day another time." Tim hugged Hazel and learned that jealousy only makes everyone sad.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Luke. One day, Luke saw mom with the dishes. At first, Luke just wanted to keep playing.

But then Luke thought, "What if that was me? I would want someone to help!" So Luke went over and asked, "Can I help you?"

The person smiled big and said, "Yes, please! That's so kind of you!" Luke helped as best as he could.

When it was done, the person said, "Thank you so much! You are a wonderful helper!" Luke felt so happy inside, happier than when playing alone.

His dad said, "I'm so proud of you for helping!" Luke learned that helping others makes everyone feel good, especially yourself.



Once upon a time, there was a joyful little boy named Ethan. Ethan loved to play in the beach. One day, his dad said he should never touch medicine bottle.

Ethan said, "Okay, dad!" But he was very curious. When dad wasn't looking, Ethan went close to medicine bottle. He thought it would be fun to explore.

But something bad happened. Ethan got lost. He started to cry and called for his dad. Dad came running and helped him.

From that day on, Ethan learned that he should always listen to his dad. Some rules are there to keep us safe.



Once upon a time, a little girl named Clara went to the playground with her grandpa. They were having a nice day together.

While her grandpa was looking at something, a stranger came up to Clara. The stranger smiled and said, "Would you like some candy? Come with me!"

Clara remembered what her grandpa had taught her. She said loudly, "No! I don't talk to strangers!" Then Clara ran back to her grandpa.

Clara told her grandpa what happened. Grandpa was so proud! "You did the right thing! Never go anywhere with someone you don't know."

Clara felt brave and safe. She learned that it's always okay to say no to strangers and run to a grown-up you trust.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Finn. Every morning, Finn didn't want to get up. He played and dawdled instead of getting ready.

One day, because Finn was so slow, he missed the school bus! His daddy had to drive him, and they were both late.

At school, Finn had missed story time, the best part of the day! He was so sad. His friends had all the fun without him.

That night, his daddy helped make a list: wake up, brush teeth, get dressed, eat breakfast. Finn put stickers on the list when he finished each thing.

The next day, Finn got ready quickly! He caught the bus and didn't miss anything. Having a routine makes mornings easier and better!



Once upon a time, a little girl named Nina wanted to make a sandcastle. She tried and tried, but it was too hard to do alone!

Then Nina's friend Tommy came by. "Need help?" asked Tommy. At first, Nina said, "No, I can do it myself!"

But after trying more and failing, Nina finally said, "Okay, please help me." Together, they started working.

With two people helping, the job became easy! They finished quickly and had so much fun doing it together. They high-fived and celebrated!

Nina learned that it's okay to ask for help. Working together makes hard things easier and more fun. Two friends are better than one!

Once upon a time, a little boy named Tim and a little girl named Chloe were playing together. They both wanted to use the bike.

"Me first!" yelled Tim. "No, me first!" yelled Chloe. They pushed and pulled, and soon they were both very upset.

An older kid saw them fighting and came over. "Why don't you take turns? One person goes, then the other person goes."

Tim went first for a little while, then it was Chloe's turn. They kept switching, and guess what? They both got to play!

Tim and Chloe learned that taking turns is fair. Everyone gets a chance, and no one feels left out. Now they always take turns and never fight!

Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Drew. One day, Drew saw a bottle on the counter. It looked like candy!

Drew reached for it, but his mom quickly took it away. "No! That's medicine, not candy!" said mom.

"But it looks yummy," said Drew. Mom sat down with Drew to explain something important.

"Medicine helps sick people feel better, but it can make healthy people very sick. Only grown-ups can give medicine, and only when someone needs it."

Drew understood now. Medicine is not a treat. He promised to never touch medicine bottles. Some things that look like candy can be dangerous!

Maya and Noah said sorry to each other. They learned to take turns and talk instead of fight. Using words is much better than fighting!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Hazel. One day, while playing in the attic, Hazel accidentally knocked over the family photo frame. It fell to the floor and broke!

Hazel was very scared. When mommy came and asked what happened, Hazel said, "I didn't do it! Maybe the wind did it!" But there was no wind inside the house.

Mommy looked at Hazel with sad eyes. "Are you telling me the truth?" Hazel looked at the floor and didn't say anything. She felt bad for lying.

Finally, Hazel said, "I'm sorry, mommy. I did it. I was playing too rough and it was an accident. I was scared to tell you."

Mommy hugged Hazel and said, "Thank you for telling the truth. Accidents happen, and I'm not angry. But lying makes things worse. Always tell the truth, even when you're scared." Hazel felt much better after being honest.

Later came and went. Before Pearl knew it, it was bedtime! She hadn't done any homework. Now it was too late, and she was very tired.

The next day at school, the teacher was disappointed that Pearl didn't have her homework. Pearl felt embarrassed and sad.

"Being greedy doesn't make you happy," said dad. "Now you don't feel good, and Pearl is sad." Theo said sorry to Pearl and learned that being greedy only makes everyone feel bad.



Once upon a time, a little girl named Zoe wanted to finish a big puzzle. She tried and tried, but it was too hard to do alone!

Then Zoe's friend Ivy came by. "Need help?" asked Ivy. At first, Zoe said, "No, I can do it myself!"

But after trying more and failing, Zoe finally said, "Okay, please help me." Together, they started working.

With two people helping, the job became easy! They finished quickly and had so much fun doing it together. They high-fived and celebrated!

Zoe learned that it's okay to ask for help. Working together makes hard things easier and more fun. Two friends are better than one!



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Oscar. Oscar was playing too rough, even though his mommy said not to.

While playing, Oscar got a scrape! It hurt a lot and Oscar started to cry. His mommy came running to help.

Mommy cleaned the boo-boo and gave Oscar a bandage. "This is why I said to be careful," mommy explained gently.

Oscar felt better after a hug and a kiss. But he learned an important lesson: the rules are there to keep him safe.

From then on, Oscar remembered to be more careful. Getting hurt is no fun, and following the rules helps avoid accidents!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Stella. Stella didn't like to listen to rules. She thought rules were boring!

One day, Stella's daddy said not to do something. But Stella didn't listen. She kept not wearing a jacket anyway.

Then something bad happened. Stella caught a cold and had to stay in bed for days. She wished she had listened!

Stella's daddy wasn't angry, just sad. "I told you because I love you and want to keep you safe," daddy said.

Stella finally understood. Rules aren't to be mean—they're to protect us! She learned that lesson the hard way. Now she listens more carefully.



Once upon a time, a little boy named Jack and a little girl named Stella were playing together. They both wanted to use the swing.

"Me first!" yelled Jack. "No, me first!" yelled Stella. They pushed and pulled, and soon they were both very upset.

An older kid saw them fighting and came over. "Why don't you take turns? One person goes, then the other person goes."

Jack went first for a little while, then it was Stella's turn. They kept switching, and guess what? They both got to play!

Jack and Stella learned that taking turns is fair. Everyone gets a chance, and no one feels left out. Now they always take turns and never fight!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Hazel. Hazel had a friend named Zach. They promised to play together at the park the next day.

But when the next day came, Hazel decided to do something else instead. She forgot all about the promise to Zach.

Zach waited and waited, but Hazel never came. Zach felt very sad and disappointed. When Hazel saw Zach later, Zach was crying.

"You promised!" said Zach. Hazel suddenly remembered and felt terrible. "I'm so sorry," said Hazel. "I forgot."

Hazel learned that promises are very important. When we break a promise, we hurt our friends. From then on, Hazel always kept her promises.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Ryan. Ryan was afraid of loud noises. Whenever he saw loud noises, he would hide!

One day, his mom said, "Let's try to be brave together." Ryan was nervous but held his mom's hand tight.

They faced loud noises slowly and carefully. At first, Ryan was still scared. But his mom was right there.

Little by little, Ryan felt less afraid. He realized that with help, loud noises wasn't so scary after all!

Ryan was so proud of being brave! He learned that it's okay to be afraid, but facing your fears makes you stronger. And having someone to help makes it easier.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Jake. One day, while playing in the attic, Jake accidentally knocked over dad's special mug. It fell to the floor and broke!

Jake was very scared. When dad came and asked what happened, Jake said, "I didn't do it! Maybe the wind did it!" But there was no wind inside the house.

Dad looked at Jake with sad eyes. "Are you telling me the truth?" Jake looked at the floor and didn't say anything. He felt bad for lying.

Finally, Jake said, "I'm sorry, dad. I did it. I was playing too rough and it was an accident. I was scared to tell you."

Dad hugged Jake and said, "Thank you for telling the truth. Accidents happen, and I'm not angry. But lying makes things worse. Always tell the truth, even when you're scared." Jake felt much better after being honest.



Once upon a time, a little girl named Nora wanted to build a tall tower with blocks. She tried and tried, but it was too hard to do alone!

Then Nora's friend Jack came by. "Need help?" asked Jack. At first, Nora said, "No, I can do it myself!"

But after trying more and failing, Nora finally said, "Okay, please help me." Together, they started working.

Nora learned that it's okay to ask for help. Working together makes hard things easier and more fun. Two friends are better than one!



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Jasper. At school, a bigger kid named Chloe was mean to him. Chloe called Jasper names and made him feel sad.

Jasper didn't want to go to school anymore. He would cry and feel scared. But he didn't tell anyone what was happening.

Finally, his dad noticed something was wrong. Jasper told them about Chloe. Together, they talked to the teacher.

The teacher helped stop the bullying. Chloe learned that being mean is wrong. Jasper learned that it's important to tell grown-ups when someone is being mean.

Jasper felt safe again! He learned that telling someone isn't tattling—it's asking for help. We should always speak up when something is wrong!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Pearl. At school, a bigger kid named Ava was mean to her. Ava called Pearl names and made her feel sad.

Pearl didn't want to go to school anymore. She would cry and feel scared. But she didn't tell anyone what was happening.

Finally, her dad noticed something was wrong. Pearl told them about Ava. Together, they talked to the teacher.

Pearl felt safe again! She learned that telling someone isn't tattling—it's asking for help. We should always speak up when something is wrong!



Once upon a time, a little boy named Adam went to the market with his grandma. There were so many exciting things to see!

Adam saw something shiny and colorful. Without thinking, he walked toward it, leaving his grandma behind. Adam walked and walked until...

He looked around and didn't see his grandma anywhere! Adam was lost! He felt very scared and started to cry.

A kind worker found Adam and helped find his grandma. When they were together again, Adam hugged his grandma so tight!

"Never wander off without me," said grandma. Adam learned to always stay close to his grandma in busy places. It's scary to be lost.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Charlie. Charlie never liked to clean up. His room was always very messy!

One day, Charlie couldn't find his lucky sock. He looked everywhere but there was so much stuff on the floor! Charlie started to cry.

His daddy said, "If you kept your room clean, you could find your things." Charlie knew daddy was right.

Together, they cleaned the whole room. They picked up toys, folded clothes, and put things in their place. And guess what? They found the lucky sock!

Charlie was so happy! He learned that keeping things clean helps you find what you need. A tidy room is a happy room!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Leah who had a brother named Henry. One day, they both wanted who sits in the front.

"It's mine!" yelled Leah. "No, it's mine!" yelled Henry. They started pushing and grabbing. Soon they were really fighting!

Mommy heard the noise and came in. "Stop!" said mommy. "Fighting is not okay!" Both Leah and Henry were in trouble.

They had to sit in time-out and think about what they did. Mommy said, "Use your words, not your hands. Talk about problems."

Leah and Henry said sorry to each other. They learned to take turns and talk instead of fight. Using words is much better than fighting!



Once upon a time, a little boy named Zach went to the park with his mom. They were having a nice day together.

While his mom was looking at something, a stranger came up to Zach. The stranger smiled and said, "Would you like some candy? Come with me!"

Zach remembered what his mom had taught him. He said loudly, "No! I don't talk to strangers!" Then Zach ran back to his mom.

Zach told his mom what happened. Mom was so proud! "You did the right thing! Never go anywhere with someone you don't know."

Zach felt brave and safe. He learned that it's always okay to say no to strangers and run to a grown-up you trust.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Flora. One day, her dad made delicious juice for Flora and her little brother Oscar.

Dad put the juice on the table. "Make sure you share nicely," said dad. But Flora wanted all the juice for herself!

When Oscar wasn't looking, Flora took most of the juice. She ate and ate until her tummy hurt very much!

Flora felt sick and couldn't play anymore. Oscar was sad because there wasn't enough juice left. Dad came and saw what happened.

"Being greedy doesn't make you happy," said dad. "Now you don't feel good, and Oscar is sad." Flora said sorry to Oscar and learned that being greedy only makes everyone feel bad.

Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Theo. Theo had a sister named Anna. One day, Anna got a pretty dress as a present.

Theo felt jealous. "Why did Anna get something and I didn't?" he thought. Theo got so angry that he took the pretty dress and hid it!

Anna couldn't find her new thing and started to cry. Dad asked, "Theo, do you know where it is?"

Theo felt bad seeing Anna so sad. He went and got the pretty dress and said, "I'm sorry. I took it because I was jealous."

Dad explained, "Everyone gets different things at different times. Anna's special day will be your special day another time." Theo hugged Anna and learned that jealousy only makes everyone sad.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Bella. Bella loved watching cartoons on the TV. She watched for hours and hours every day.

Her mommy said, "You watch too much TV. Go play outside!" But Bella didn't want to stop.

After many days of too much TV, Bella's head started to hurt. Her eyes felt tired. She didn't feel good at all.

The doctor said Bella needed to rest her eyes and play more. So Bella went outside and discovered how fun it was to run and play!

Bella learned that too much TV isn't good for you. Playing outside and using your imagination is much more fun. Now Bella only watches a little TV each day.

Later came and went. Before Tommy knew it, it was bedtime! He hadn't done any homework. Now it was too late, and he was very tired.

The next day at school, the teacher was disappointed that Tommy didn't have his homework. Tommy felt embarrassed and sad.

After that, Tommy learned to do homework first, then play. When you finish your work first, you can play without worrying! Work first, then play—that's the best way!

Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Mia. One day, Mia saw a bottle on the counter. It looked like candy!

"But it looks yummy," said Mia. Mommy sat down with Mia to explain something important.

"Medicine helps sick people feel better, but it can make healthy people very sick. Only grown-ups can give medicine, and only when someone needs it."

Mia understood now. Medicine is not a treat. She promised to never touch medicine bottles. Some things that look like candy can be dangerous!

Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Henry. One day, Henry saw matches on the table. They looked interesting!

Henry understood now. Fire is very serious. Only grown-ups can use things that make fire. He promised to never touch matches or lighters.

The next day at school, the teacher was disappointed that Emma didn't have her homework. Emma felt embarrassed and sad.

After that, Emma learned to do homework first, then play. When you finish your work first, you can play without worrying! Work first, then play—that's the best way!



Once upon a time, a little boy named Ethan loved going to the playground. His favorite thing was the slide.

One day, Ethan wanted to show off. He climbed higher than he should and hung upside down in a silly way. "Look at me!" he yelled.

But then Ethan lost his grip and fell! He hurt his arm and started to cry. His mom came running.

At the doctor, they said Ethan's arm would be okay, but he had to wear a bandage and rest. Ethan couldn't play for a whole week!

Ethan learned that playground rules are there to keep us safe. Showing off and being silly on equipment can lead to getting hurt. Play safe, have fun!



Once upon a time, a little girl named Violet went to the pond with her grandpa. It was a hot day and the water looked so inviting!

Her grandpa said, "Wait for me before going in the water." But Violet was too excited. She ran and jumped right in!

The water was deeper than Violet thought! She couldn't touch the bottom and got scared. She started to splash and cry for help.

Her grandpa quickly jumped in and pulled Violet out. They were both very shaken up.

Violet learned an important lesson that day. Water can be dangerous! Always wait for a grown-up, and never swim alone. Now Violet always asks for permission before going near water.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Oscar. Oscar was afraid of dogs. Whenever he saw dogs, he would hide!

One day, his daddy said, "Let's try to be brave together." Oscar was nervous but held his daddy's hand tight.

They faced dogs slowly and carefully. At first, Oscar was still scared. But his daddy was right there.

Little by little, Oscar felt less afraid. He realized that with help, dogs wasn't so scary after all!

Oscar was so proud of being brave! He learned that it's okay to be afraid, but facing your fears makes you stronger. And having someone to help makes it easier.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Sara. Sara was playing with scissors, even though her daddy said not to.

While playing, Sara fell down! It hurt a lot and Sara started to cry. Her daddy came running to help.

Daddy cleaned the boo-boo and gave Sara a bandage. "This is why I said to be careful," daddy explained gently.

Sara felt better after a hug and a kiss. But she learned an important lesson: the rules are there to keep her safe.

From then on, Sara remembered to be more careful. Getting hurt is no fun, and following the rules helps avoid accidents!



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Henry. Henry didn't like to listen to rules. He thought rules were boring!

One day, Henry's dad said not to do something. But Henry didn't listen. He kept playing too close to the road anyway.

Then something bad happened. Henry almost got hit by a car and was very scared. He wished he had listened!

Henry's dad wasn't angry, just sad. "I told you because I love you and want to keep you safe," dad said.

Henry finally understood. Rules aren't to be mean—they're to protect us! He learned that lesson the hard way. Now he listens more carefully.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Ava. Ava only wanted to eat chips. "I don't like fruits!" she would say every day.

Her daddy tried to give Ava healthy food, but Ava always said no. She only ate chips for days and days.

Soon, Ava didn't feel good. Her tummy hurt and she had no energy to play. The doctor said Ava needed to eat healthy food to feel better.

Ava tried the fruits, just a tiny bite. Hey, it wasn't so bad! Actually, it was pretty good! She tried more healthy foods and started feeling much better.

Now Ava eats lots of good food that makes her strong. She still has treats sometimes, but she knows healthy food is important!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Hazel who had a brother named Felix. One day, they both wanted who sits in the front.

"It's mine!" yelled Hazel. "No, it's mine!" yelled Felix. They started pushing and grabbing. Soon they were really fighting!

Mommy heard the noise and came in. "Stop!" said mommy. "Fighting is not okay!" Both Hazel and Felix were in trouble.

They had to sit in time-out and think about what they did. Mommy said, "Use your words, not your hands. Talk about problems."

Hazel and Felix said sorry to each other. They learned to take turns and talk instead of fight. Using words is much better than fighting!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Daisy. One day, Daisy saw matches on the table. They looked interesting!

Daisy reached for the matches, but her dad quickly stopped her. "No! Those are very dangerous!" said dad.

Dad sat down with Daisy and explained. "Fire is not a toy. Matches and lighters can start fires that hurt people and burn things."

"If you ever see fire or smoke, you should tell a grown-up right away. And remember: Stop, Drop, and Roll if your clothes catch fire."

Daisy understood now. Fire is very serious. Only grown-ups can use things that make fire. She promised to never touch matches or lighters.

Later, Emma saw a child who had no toys at all. That child looked at Emma's book and said, "Wow, you're so lucky!"

Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Leah. Leah never wanted to go to bed. "I'm not tired!" she always said.

One night, Leah stayed up very, very late playing with toys. Her mom said, "Time for bed!" But Leah hid under the covers and kept playing.

The next day, Leah was so tired! She couldn't run. She couldn't play. She fell asleep at breakfast!

Her mom said, "This is why we need sleep. Our bodies need rest to play and have fun."

That night, Leah went to bed on time. The next day, she had so much energy! Leah learned that sleep helps us feel good and have fun. Now bedtime isn't so bad!



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Milo. One day, Milo saw a friend who lost a toy. At first, Milo just wanted to keep playing.

But then Milo thought, "What if that was me? I would want someone to help!" So Milo went over and asked, "Can I help you?"

The person smiled big and said, "Yes, please! That's so kind of you!" Milo helped as best as he could.

When it was done, the person said, "Thank you so much! You are a wonderful helper!" Milo felt so happy inside, happier than when playing alone.

His dad said, "I'm so proud of you for helping!" Milo learned that helping others makes everyone feel good, especially yourself.



Once upon a time, a little boy named Hugo went to the store with his mommy. There were so many exciting things to see!

Hugo saw something shiny and colorful. Without thinking, he walked toward it, leaving his mommy behind. Hugo walked and walked until...

He looked around and didn't see his mommy anywhere! Hugo was lost! He felt very scared and started to cry.

A kind worker found Hugo and helped find his mommy. When they were together again, Hugo hugged his mommy so tight!

"Never wander off without me," said mommy. Hugo learned to always stay close to his mommy in busy places. It's scary to be lost.

Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Ivy. Every morning, Ivy didn't want to get up. She played and dawdled instead of getting ready.

The next day, Ivy got ready quickly! She caught the bus and didn't miss anything. Having a routine makes mornings easier and better!

Tim felt brave and safe. He learned that it's always okay to say no to strangers and run to a grown-up you trust.

Adam said, "Okay, daddy!" But he was very curious. When daddy wasn't looking, Adam went close to broken glass. He thought it would be fun to explore.

But something bad happened. Adam made someone cry. He started to cry and called for his daddy. Daddy came running and helped him.

Adam felt very sorry. He hugged his daddy and said, "I'm sorry I didn't listen." Daddy said, "I told you because I love you and want you to be safe."

From that day on, Adam learned that he should always listen to his daddy. Some rules are there to keep us safe.

At school, Sophie had missed story time, the best part of the day! She was so sad. Her friends had all the fun without her.

That night, her mommy helped make a list: wake up, brush teeth, get dressed, eat breakfast. Sophie put stickers on the list when she finished each thing.

The next day, Sophie got ready quickly! She caught the bus and didn't miss anything. Having a routine makes mornings easier and better!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Rose. Rose was afraid of water. Whenever she saw water, she would hide!

One day, her dad said, "Let's try to be brave together." Rose was nervous but held her dad's hand tight.

They faced water slowly and carefully. At first, Rose was still scared. But her dad was right there.

Little by little, Rose felt less afraid. She realized that with help, water wasn't so scary after all!

Rose was so proud of being brave! She learned that it's okay to be afraid, but facing your fears makes you stronger. And having someone to help makes it easier.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Violet. At school, a bigger kid named Felix was mean to her. Felix called Violet names and made her feel sad.

Violet didn't want to go to school anymore. She would cry and feel scared. But she didn't tell anyone what was happening.

Finally, her dad noticed something was wrong. Violet told them about Felix. Together, they talked to the teacher.

The teacher helped stop the bullying. Felix learned that being mean is wrong. Violet learned that it's important to tell grown-ups when someone is being mean.

Violet felt safe again! She learned that telling someone isn't tattling—it's asking for help. We should always speak up when something is wrong!



Once upon a time, a little boy named Ryan wanted to make a sandcastle. He tried and tried, but it was too hard to do alone!

Then Ryan's friend Hazel came by. "Need help?" asked Hazel. At first, Ryan said, "No, I can do it myself!"

But after trying more and failing, Ryan finally said, "Okay, please help me." Together, they started working.

With two people helping, the job became easy! They finished quickly and had so much fun doing it together. They high-fived and celebrated!

Ryan learned that it's okay to ask for help. Working together makes hard things easier and more fun. Two friends are better than one!



Once upon a time, a sweet little boy named Jasper went to the backyard with his daddy. Jasper loved to explore and discover new things.

While walking, Jasper saw a dark cave. It looked exciting! He forgot what his daddy said about staying close. Jasper ran toward it to take a closer look.

"Stop!" yelled his daddy. But Jasper got too close and almost fell in! His daddy grabbed him just in time.

Jasper's heart was beating fast. He was very scared. "Daddy, I'm sorry," Jasper said with tears in his eyes.

His daddy hugged Jasper tight. "I'm glad you're safe. Some places are dangerous, and that's why we must be careful." Jasper promised to always listen and never wander off again.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Owen. One day, while playing in their room, Owen accidentally knocked over grandma's old clock. It fell to the floor and broke!

Owen was very scared. When mommy came and asked what happened, Owen said, "I didn't do it! Maybe the wind did it!" But there was no wind inside the house.

Mommy looked at Owen with sad eyes. "Are you telling me the truth?" Owen looked at the floor and didn't say anything. He felt bad for lying.

Finally, Owen said, "I'm sorry, mommy. I did it. I was playing too rough and it was an accident. I was scared to tell you."

Mommy hugged Owen and said, "Thank you for telling the truth. Accidents happen, and I'm not angry. But lying makes things worse. Always tell the truth, even when you're scared." Owen felt much better after being honest.



Once upon a time, a little boy named Hugo wanted to carry heavy boxes. He tried and tried, but it was too hard to do alone!

Then Hugo's friend Eli came by. "Need help?" asked Eli. At first, Hugo said, "No, I can do it myself!"

But after trying more and failing, Hugo finally said, "Okay, please help me." Together, they started working.

With two people helping, the job became easy! They finished quickly and had so much fun doing it together. They high-fived and celebrated!

Hugo learned that it's okay to ask for help. Working together makes hard things easier and more fun. Two friends are better than one!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Maya. One day, Maya saw a bottle on the counter. It looked like candy!

Maya reached for it, but her dad quickly took it away. "No! That's medicine, not candy!" said dad.

"But it looks yummy," said Maya. Dad sat down with Maya to explain something important.

"Medicine helps sick people feel better, but it can make healthy people very sick. Only grown-ups can give medicine, and only when someone needs it."

Maya understood now. Medicine is not a treat. She promised to never touch medicine bottles. Some things that look like candy can be dangerous!



Once upon a time, a little boy named Jack went to the hiking trail with his daddy. Jack loved exploring and seeing all the plants and animals.

While walking, Jack saw a bird's nest. It looked so cool! Jack wanted to touch it and take it home.

But his daddy said, "Wait! We should only look, not touch. Some things in nature can be dangerous or need to stay where they are."

Daddy explained that touching the wrong things could hurt Jack or the animals. "We're just visitors here. We should respect nature."

Jack understood. He took pictures with his eyes instead of his hands. Looking is wonderful too! Jack learned to enjoy nature safely and respectfully.

"I don't want to wait! I want it now!" said Zach. He started to stomp his feet and whine.

But being impatient didn't help. It just made Zach feel worse. his daddy said, "Being upset won't make time go faster."

"Waiting wasn't so bad!" said Zach with a big smile. He learned that being patient and finding fun things to do makes waiting easier. Good things come to those who wait!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Zoe. After school, Zoe was supposed to do homework. But she wanted to watch TV instead!

"I'll do it later!" said Zoe, running off to play. Her mommy called, "Remember your homework!" But Zoe didn't listen.

Later came and went. Before Zoe knew it, it was bedtime! She hadn't done any homework. Now it was too late, and she was very tired.

The next day at school, the teacher was disappointed that Zoe didn't have her homework. Zoe felt embarrassed and sad.

After that, Zoe learned to do homework first, then play. When you finish your work first, you can play without worrying! Work first, then play—that's the best way!



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Max. One day, Max heard some big kids say a word that sounded funny. So Max said it too!

His daddy's face looked very surprised and sad. "Where did you learn that word?" asked daddy. "That's a bad word that hurts people's feelings."

Max didn't know! He just thought it sounded funny. But now he understood that some words can make people feel bad.

Daddy explained, "Kind words make people happy. Mean words make people sad. We always want to use kind words."

Max felt sorry for saying the bad word. He learned to think before speaking. Now Max uses kind words that make people smile!

Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Luke. One day, Luke saw matches on the table. They looked interesting!

Luke reached for the matches, but his mommy quickly stopped him. "No! Those are very dangerous!" said mommy.

Mommy sat down with Luke and explained. "Fire is not a toy. Matches and lighters can start fires that hurt people and burn things."

"If you ever see fire or smoke, you should tell a grown-up right away. And remember: Stop, Drop, and Roll if your clothes catch fire."

Luke understood now. Fire is very serious. Only grown-ups can use things that make fire. He promised to never touch matches or lighters.

Together, they cleaned the whole room. They picked up toys, folded clothes, and put things in their place. And guess what? They found the beloved teddy bear!

Anna was so happy! She learned that keeping things clean helps you find what you need. A tidy room is a happy room!

Tommy reached for the matches, but his daddy quickly stopped him. "No! Those are very dangerous!" said daddy.

Daddy sat down with Tommy and explained. "Fire is not a toy. Matches and lighters can start fires that hurt people and burn things."

"If you ever see fire or smoke, you should tell a grown-up right away. And remember: Stop, Drop, and Roll if your clothes catch fire."

Tommy understood now. Fire is very serious. Only grown-ups can use things that make fire. He promised to never touch matches or lighters.



Once upon a time, a little boy named Jasper wanted to carry heavy boxes. He tried and tried, but it was too hard to do alone!

Then Jasper's friend Leo came by. "Need help?" asked Leo. At first, Jasper said, "No, I can do it myself!"

But after trying more and failing, Jasper finally said, "Okay, please help me." Together, they started working.

With two people helping, the job became easy! They finished quickly and had so much fun doing it together. They high-fived and celebrated!

Jasper learned that it's okay to ask for help. Working together makes hard things easier and more fun. Two friends are better than one!



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Adam. Adam loved watching cartoons on the TV. He watched for hours and hours every day.

His dad said, "You watch too much TV. Go play outside!" But Adam didn't want to stop.

After many days of too much TV, Adam's head started to hurt. His eyes felt tired. He didn't feel good at all.

The doctor said Adam needed to rest his eyes and play more. So Adam went outside and discovered how fun it was to run and play!

Adam learned that too much TV isn't good for you. Playing outside and using your imagination is much more fun. Now Adam only watches a little TV each day.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Ava. Ava was jumping on furniture, even though her daddy said not to.

While playing, Ava twisted their ankle! It hurt a lot and Ava started to cry. Her daddy came running to help.

Daddy cleaned the boo-boo and gave Ava a bandage. "This is why I said to be careful," daddy explained gently.

Ava felt better after a hug and a kiss. But she learned an important lesson: the rules are there to keep her safe.

From then on, Ava remembered to be more careful. Getting hurt is no fun, and following the rules helps avoid accidents!



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Jake. Jake only wanted to eat cookies. "I don't like fruits!" he would say every day.

His daddy tried to give Jake healthy food, but Jake always said no. He only ate cookies for days and days.

Soon, Jake didn't feel good. His tummy hurt and he had no energy to play. The doctor said Jake needed to eat healthy food to feel better.

Jake tried the fruits, just a tiny bite. Hey, it wasn't so bad! Actually, it was pretty good! He tried more healthy foods and started feeling much better.

Now Jake eats lots of good food that makes him strong. He still has treats sometimes, but he knows healthy food is important!



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Felix. One day, Felix saw a bottle on the counter. It looked like candy!

Felix reached for it, but his dad quickly took it away. "No! That's medicine, not candy!" said dad.

"But it looks yummy," said Felix. Dad sat down with Felix to explain something important.

"Medicine helps sick people feel better, but it can make healthy people very sick. Only grown-ups can give medicine, and only when someone needs it."

Felix understood now. Medicine is not a treat. He promised to never touch medicine bottles. Some things that look like candy can be dangerous!



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Jasper. One day, Jasper saw an old lady with heavy bags. At first, Jasper just wanted to keep playing.

But then Jasper thought, "What if that was me? I would want someone to help!" So Jasper went over and asked, "Can I help you?"

The person smiled big and said, "Yes, please! That's so kind of you!" Jasper helped as best as he could.

When it was done, the person said, "Thank you so much! You are a wonderful helper!" Jasper felt so happy inside, happier than when playing alone.

His dad said, "I'm so proud of you for helping!" Jasper learned that helping others makes everyone feel good, especially yourself.



Once upon a time, a little girl named Nina went to the market with her dad. There were so many exciting things to see!

Nina saw something shiny and colorful. Without thinking, she walked toward it, leaving her dad behind. Nina walked and walked until...

She looked around and didn't see her dad anywhere! Nina was lost! She felt very scared and started to cry.

A kind worker found Nina and helped find her dad. When they were together again, Nina hugged her dad so tight!

"Never wander off without me," said dad. Nina learned to always stay close to her dad in busy places. It's scary to be lost.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Ivy. Ivy never wanted to go to bed. "I'm not tired!" she always said.

One night, Ivy stayed up very, very late playing with toys. Her mom said, "Time for bed!" But Ivy hid under the covers and kept playing.

The next day, Ivy was so tired! She couldn't run. She couldn't play. She fell asleep at breakfast!

Her mom said, "This is why we need sleep. Our bodies need rest to play and have fun."

That night, Ivy went to bed on time. The next day, she had so much energy! Ivy learned that sleep helps us feel good and have fun. Now bedtime isn't so bad!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Daisy. One day, Daisy saw a little kid who fell down. At first, Daisy just wanted to keep playing.

But then Daisy thought, "What if that was me? I would want someone to help!" So Daisy went over and asked, "Can I help you?"

The person smiled big and said, "Yes, please! That's so kind of you!" Daisy helped as best as she could.

Once upon a time, a friendly little girl named Emma went to the meadow with her grandma. Emma loved to explore and discover new things.

While walking, Emma saw a busy street. It looked exciting! She forgot what her grandma said about staying close. Emma ran toward it to take a closer look.

"Stop!" yelled her grandma. But Emma got too close and almost fell in! Her grandma grabbed her just in time.

Emma's heart was beating fast. She was very scared. "Grandma, I'm sorry," Emma said with tears in her eyes.

Her grandma hugged Emma tight. "I'm glad you're safe. Some places are dangerous, and that's why we must be careful." Emma promised to always listen and never wander off again.



Once upon a time, a little boy named Theo and a little boy named Tim were playing together. They both wanted to use the swing.

"Me first!" yelled Theo. "No, me first!" yelled Tim. They pushed and pulled, and soon they were both very upset.

An older kid saw them fighting and came over. "Why don't you take turns? One person goes, then the other person goes."

Theo went first for a little while, then it was Tim's turn. They kept switching, and guess what? They both got to play!

Theo and Tim learned that taking turns is fair. Everyone gets a chance, and no one feels left out. Now they always take turns and never fight!



Once upon a time, a little boy named Archie loved going to the playground. His favorite thing was the slide.

One day, Archie wanted to show off. He climbed higher than he should and hung upside down in a silly way. "Look at me!" he yelled.

But then Archie lost his grip and fell! He hurt his arm and started to cry. His mom came running.

At the doctor, they said Archie's arm would be okay, but he had to wear a bandage and rest. Archie couldn't play for a whole week!

Archie learned that playground rules are there to keep us safe. Showing off and being silly on equipment can lead to getting hurt. Play safe, have fun!

Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Alfie. One day, his mom made delicious sandwiches for Alfie and his little sister Stella.

When Stella wasn't looking, Alfie took most of the sandwiches. He ate and ate until his tummy hurt very much!

Alfie felt sick and couldn't play anymore. Stella was sad because there wasn't enough sandwiches left. Mom came and saw what happened.

"Being greedy doesn't make you happy," said mom. "Now you don't feel good, and Stella is sad." Alfie said sorry to Stella and learned that being greedy only makes everyone feel bad.



Once upon a time, a little boy named Charlie went to the pool with his daddy. It was a hot day and the water looked so inviting!

His daddy said, "Wait for me before going in the water." But Charlie was too excited. He ran and jumped right in!

The water was deeper than Charlie thought! He couldn't touch the bottom and got scared. He started to splash and cry for help.

His daddy quickly jumped in and pulled Charlie out. They were both very shaken up.

Charlie learned an important lesson that day. Water can be dangerous! Always wait for a grown-up, and never swim alone. Now Charlie always asks for permission before going near water.

Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Ruby. One day, while playing in the attic, Ruby accidentally knocked over mom's pretty bowl. It fell to the floor and broke!

Ruby was very scared. When dad came and asked what happened, Ruby said, "I didn't do it! Maybe the wind did it!" But there was no wind inside the house.

Dad looked at Ruby with sad eyes. "Are you telling me the truth?" Ruby looked at the floor and didn't say anything. She felt bad for lying.

Finally, Ruby said, "I'm sorry, dad. I did it. I was playing too rough and it was an accident. I was scared to tell you."

Dad hugged Ruby and said, "Thank you for telling the truth. Accidents happen, and I'm not angry. But lying makes things worse. Always tell the truth, even when you're scared." Ruby felt much better after being honest.

Suddenly, Maya tripped and fell! She scraped her knee and it hurt a lot. Maya started to cry.

Her mommy came and put a bandage on the scrape. "This is why I asked you to slow down," said mommy gently.

Maya's knee hurt for several days. She learned that rushing can lead to accidents. It's better to slow down and be careful than to get hurt.

Her mommy's face looked very surprised and sad. "Where did you learn that word?" asked mommy. "That's a bad word that hurts people's feelings."

Mia didn't know! She just thought it sounded funny. But now she understood that some words can make people feel bad.

Mommy explained, "Kind words make people happy. Mean words make people sad. We always want to use kind words."

Mia felt sorry for saying the bad word. She learned to think before speaking. Now Mia uses kind words that make people smile!

Once upon a time, a little boy named Ryan went to the store with his dad. They were having a nice day together.

While his dad was looking at something, a stranger came up to Ryan. The stranger smiled and said, "Would you like some candy? Come with me!"

Ryan remembered what his dad had taught him. He said loudly, "No! I don't talk to strangers!" Then Ryan ran back to his dad.

Ryan told his dad what happened. Dad was so proud! "You did the right thing! Never go anywhere with someone you don't know."

Ryan felt brave and safe. He learned that it's always okay to say no to strangers and run to a grown-up you trust.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Sophie. Sophie had a favorite spinning top that she loved very much. She played with it every day.

Later, Ryan saw a child who had no toys at all. That child looked at Ryan's toy and said, "Wow, you're so lucky!"

Ryan suddenly felt bad for complaining. He realized that having any gift is special. His mom worked hard to give him something nice.

Ryan ran to his mom and said, "Thank you for my gift! I love it!" He learned to be grateful for what he has. Being thankful makes everyone happier!

Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Ava who had a little hamster named Teddy. Ava loved Teddy very much.

One day, Ava was supposed to give Teddy food and water. But Ava was busy playing with toys and said, "I'll do it later!"

Later came and went, but Ava forgot all about Teddy. The little hamster got very hungry and thirsty. Teddy made sad little sounds.

Ava's mom said, "Did you feed Teddy?" Ava suddenly remembered and felt very bad. She ran to feed and give water to the hamster.

"Teddy depends on you," said her parent. "Pets need us to take care of them." Ava promised to always remember to care for Teddy first, because pets are family too.



Once upon a time, a little boy named Jack went to the park with his daddy. Jack loved exploring and seeing all the plants and animals.

While walking, Jack saw berries on a bush. It looked so cool! Jack wanted to touch it and take it home.

But his daddy said, "Wait! We should only look, not touch. Some things in nature can be dangerous or need to stay where they are."

Daddy explained that touching the wrong things could hurt Jack or the animals. "We're just visitors here. We should respect nature."

Jack understood. He took pictures with his eyes instead of his hands. Looking is wonderful too! Jack learned to enjoy nature safely and respectfully.

Stella was so happy! She learned that keeping things clean helps you find what you need. A tidy room is a happy room!

Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Luna. Luna had a favorite doll that she loved very much. She played with it every day.

One day, her little brother Owen came and asked, "Can I play with your doll?" But Luna said, "No! It's mine! Go away!"

Owen was very sad and started to cry. Luna kept playing alone, but it didn't feel fun anymore. She saw how sad Owen was and felt bad inside.

Finally, Luna went to Owen and said, "I'm sorry. We can play together." Owen's face lit up with a big smile. They played with the doll together and had so much more fun!

Luna learned that sharing makes everyone happy. When we share, we make more friends and have more fun.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Jasper. Jasper had a sister named Ava. One day, Ava got a fun game as a present.

Jasper felt jealous. "Why did Ava get something and I didn't?" he thought. Jasper got so angry that he took the fun game and hid it!

Ava couldn't find her new thing and started to cry. Mom asked, "Jasper, do you know where it is?"

Jasper felt bad seeing Ava so sad. He went and got the fun game and said, "I'm sorry. I took it because I was jealous."

Mom explained, "Everyone gets different things at different times. Ava's special day will be your special day another time." Jasper hugged Ava and learned that jealousy only makes everyone sad.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Drew. One day, Drew said something mean to his friend Henry. Henry was very sad.

At first, Drew didn't want to say sorry. He felt embarrassed and a little stubborn. But Henry wouldn't play with him anymore.

Drew's dad said, "When we hurt someone, we need to say sorry. It helps fix the hurt."

Drew found Henry and said, "I'm really sorry for what I did. It was wrong. Can you forgive me?" Henry smiled and said yes.

They hugged and played together again! Drew learned that saying sorry is hard but important. It makes friendships strong and helps everyone feel better.

Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Flora. After school, Flora was supposed to do homework. But she wanted to play video games instead!

"I'll do it later!" said Flora, running off to play. Her dad called, "Remember your homework!" But Flora didn't listen.

Later came and went. Before Flora knew it, it was bedtime! She hadn't done any homework. Now it was too late, and she was very tired.

The next day at school, the teacher was disappointed that Flora didn't have her homework. Flora felt embarrassed and sad.

After that, Flora learned to do homework first, then play. When you finish your work first, you can play without worrying! Work first, then play—that's the best way!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Ava. One day, Ava saw a friend who lost a toy. At first, Ava just wanted to keep playing.

Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Liam. One day, Liam saw matches on the table. They looked interesting!

Liam reached for the matches, but his mommy quickly stopped him. "No! Those are very dangerous!" said mommy.

Mommy sat down with Liam and explained. "Fire is not a toy. Matches and lighters can start fires that hurt people and burn things."

"If you ever see fire or smoke, you should tell a grown-up right away. And remember: Stop, Drop, and Roll if your clothes catch fire."

Liam understood now. Fire is very serious. Only grown-ups can use things that make fire. He promised to never touch matches or lighters.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Cole. Cole was always in a hurry. He never wanted to slow down!

One day, his dad said, "Be careful! Don't go so fast!" But Cole didn't listen. He was skating without looking, going faster and faster.

Suddenly, Cole tripped and fell! He scraped his knee and it hurt a lot. Cole started to cry.

His dad came and put a bandage on the scrape. "This is why I asked you to slow down," said dad gently.

Cole's knee hurt for several days. He learned that rushing can lead to accidents. It's better to slow down and be careful than to get hurt.

"Never wander off without me," said grandpa. Mia learned to always stay close to her grandpa in busy places. It's scary to be lost.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Owen who had a sister named Chloe. One day, they both wanted a toy.

"It's mine!" yelled Owen. "No, it's mine!" yelled Chloe. They started pushing and grabbing. Soon they were really fighting!

Mommy heard the noise and came in. "Stop!" said mommy. "Fighting is not okay!" Both Owen and Chloe were in trouble.

They had to sit in time-out and think about what they did. Mommy said, "Use your words, not your hands. Talk about problems."

Owen and Chloe said sorry to each other. They learned to take turns and talk instead of fight. Using words is much better than fighting!

Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Jasper who had a special toy plane. It was his favorite toy in the whole world!

But Jasper didn't take good care of it. He left it outside in the rain, threw it around, and never put it away nicely.

Jasper learned to take care of his things. He puts toys away nicely now and treats them gently. Taking care of our things makes them last longer!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Maya. For her birthday, Maya got art supplies from her mom.

But Maya wasn't happy. "This isn't what I wanted!" she complained. "I wanted something else!" Her mom looked very sad.

Later, Maya saw a child who had no toys at all. That child looked at Maya's art supplies and said, "Wow, you're so lucky!"

Maya suddenly felt bad for complaining. She realized that having any gift is special. Her mom worked hard to give her something nice.

Maya ran to her mom and said, "Thank you for my gift! I love it!" She learned to be grateful for what she has. Being thankful makes everyone happier!



Once upon a time, a little boy named Owen went to the store with his daddy. They were having a nice day together.

While his daddy was looking at something, a stranger came up to Owen. The stranger smiled and said, "Would you like some candy? Come with me!"

Owen remembered what his daddy had taught him. He said loudly, "No! I don't talk to strangers!" Then Owen ran back to his daddy.

Owen told his daddy what happened. Daddy was so proud! "You did the right thing! Never go anywhere with someone you don't know."

Owen felt brave and safe. He learned that it's always okay to say no to strangers and run to a grown-up you trust.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Mia. Mia was afraid of dogs. Whenever she saw dogs, she would hide!
