They faced dogs slowly and carefully. At first, Mia was still scared. But her daddy was right there.

Little by little, Mia felt less afraid. She realized that with help, dogs wasn't so scary after all!

Mia was so proud of being brave! She learned that it's okay to be afraid, but facing your fears makes you stronger. And having someone to help makes it easier.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Milo. Milo was very excited about to go to the park. But his daddy said he had to wait.

"I don't want to wait! I want it now!" said Milo. He started to stomp his feet and whine.

But being impatient didn't help. It just made Milo feel worse. his daddy said, "Being upset won't make time go faster."

Milo tried to be patient. He played with toys and helped his daddy. Before Milo knew it, it was time!

"Waiting wasn't so bad!" said Milo with a big smile. He learned that being patient and finding fun things to do makes waiting easier. Good things come to those who wait!



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Alfie. Every morning, Alfie didn't want to get up. He played and dawdled instead of getting ready.

One day, because Alfie was so slow, he missed the school bus! His mommy had to drive him, and they were both late.

At school, Alfie had missed story time, the best part of the day! He was so sad. His friends had all the fun without him.

That night, his mommy helped make a list: wake up, brush teeth, get dressed, eat breakfast. Alfie put stickers on the list when he finished each thing.

The next day, Alfie got ready quickly! He caught the bus and didn't miss anything. Having a routine makes mornings easier and better!

Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Ethan who had a little puppy named Biscuit. Ethan loved Biscuit very much.

"Biscuit depends on you," said his parent. "Pets need us to take care of them." Ethan promised to always remember to care for Biscuit first, because pets are family too.

Once upon a time, a little boy named Ethan went to the forest with his grandpa. Ethan loved exploring and seeing all the plants and animals.

Grandpa explained that touching the wrong things could hurt Ethan or the animals. "We're just visitors here. We should respect nature."

Ethan understood. He took pictures with his eyes instead of his hands. Looking is wonderful too! Ethan learned to enjoy nature safely and respectfully.

Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Flora. Flora didn't like to listen to rules. She thought rules were boring!

One day, Flora's dad said not to do something. But Flora didn't listen. She kept playing too close to the road anyway.

Then something bad happened. Flora almost got hit by a car and was very scared. She wished she had listened!

Flora's dad wasn't angry, just sad. "I told you because I love you and want to keep you safe," dad said.

Flora finally understood. Rules aren't to be mean—they're to protect us! She learned that lesson the hard way. Now she listens more carefully.



Once upon a time, a little boy named Alfie went to the hiking trail with his mommy. Alfie loved exploring and seeing all the plants and animals.

While walking, Alfie saw mushrooms. It looked so cool! Alfie wanted to touch it and take it home.

But his mommy said, "Wait! We should only look, not touch. Some things in nature can be dangerous or need to stay where they are."

Mommy explained that touching the wrong things could hurt Alfie or the animals. "We're just visitors here. We should respect nature."

Alfie understood. He took pictures with his eyes instead of his hands. Looking is wonderful too! Alfie learned to enjoy nature safely and respectfully.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Owen. One day, Owen saw a bottle on the counter. It looked like candy!

Owen reached for it, but his daddy quickly took it away. "No! That's medicine, not candy!" said daddy.

"But it looks yummy," said Owen. Daddy sat down with Owen to explain something important.

"Medicine helps sick people feel better, but it can make healthy people very sick. Only grown-ups can give medicine, and only when someone needs it."

Owen understood now. Medicine is not a treat. He promised to never touch medicine bottles. Some things that look like candy can be dangerous!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Bella. Bella never wanted to go to bed. "I'm not tired!" she always said.

One night, Bella stayed up very, very late playing with toys. Her dad said, "Time for bed!" But Bella hid under the covers and kept playing.

The next day, Bella was so tired! She couldn't run. She couldn't play. She fell asleep at breakfast!

Her dad said, "This is why we need sleep. Our bodies need rest to play and have fun."

That night, Bella went to bed on time. The next day, she had so much energy! Bella learned that sleep helps us feel good and have fun. Now bedtime isn't so bad!



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Alfie. Alfie was very excited about a yummy treat. But his daddy said he had to wait.

"I don't want to wait! I want it now!" said Alfie. He started to stomp his feet and whine.

But being impatient didn't help. It just made Alfie feel worse. his daddy said, "Being upset won't make time go faster."

Alfie tried to be patient. He played with toys and helped his daddy. Before Alfie knew it, it was time!

"Waiting wasn't so bad!" said Alfie with a big smile. He learned that being patient and finding fun things to do makes waiting easier. Good things come to those who wait!



Once upon a time, a little boy named Alfie went to the fair with his daddy. There were so many exciting things to see!

Alfie saw something shiny and colorful. Without thinking, he walked toward it, leaving his daddy behind. Alfie walked and walked until...

He looked around and didn't see his daddy anywhere! Alfie was lost! He felt very scared and started to cry.

A kind worker found Alfie and helped find his daddy. When they were together again, Alfie hugged his daddy so tight!

"Never wander off without me," said daddy. Alfie learned to always stay close to his daddy in busy places. It's scary to be lost.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Archie. One day, Archie heard some big kids say a word that sounded funny. So Archie said it too!

His daddy's face looked very surprised and sad. "Where did you learn that word?" asked daddy. "That's a bad word that hurts people's feelings."

Archie didn't know! He just thought it sounded funny. But now he understood that some words can make people feel bad.

Daddy explained, "Kind words make people happy. Mean words make people sad. We always want to use kind words."

Archie felt sorry for saying the bad word. He learned to think before speaking. Now Archie uses kind words that make people smile!



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Jake. Jake was very excited about a yummy treat. But his daddy said he had to wait.

"I don't want to wait! I want it now!" said Jake. He started to stomp his feet and whine.

But being impatient didn't help. It just made Jake feel worse. his daddy said, "Being upset won't make time go faster."

Jake tried to be patient. He played with toys and helped his daddy. Before Jake knew it, it was time!

"Waiting wasn't so bad!" said Jake with a big smile. He learned that being patient and finding fun things to do makes waiting easier. Good things come to those who wait!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Leah. Leah was always in a hurry. She never wanted to slow down!

One day, her mommy said, "Be careful! Don't go so fast!" But Leah didn't listen. She was running by the pool, going faster and faster.

Suddenly, Leah tripped and fell! She scraped her knee and it hurt a lot. Leah started to cry.

Her mommy came and put a bandage on the scrape. "This is why I asked you to slow down," said mommy gently.

Leah's knee hurt for several days. She learned that rushing can lead to accidents. It's better to slow down and be careful than to get hurt.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Zach. After school, Zach was supposed to do homework. But he wanted to play with toys instead!

"I'll do it later!" said Zach, running off to play. His daddy called, "Remember your homework!" But Zach didn't listen.

Later came and went. Before Zach knew it, it was bedtime! He hadn't done any homework. Now it was too late, and he was very tired.

The next day at school, the teacher was disappointed that Zach didn't have his homework. Zach felt embarrassed and sad.

After that, Zach learned to do homework first, then play. When you finish your work first, you can play without worrying! Work first, then play—that's the best way!



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Leo. One day, Leo heard some big kids say a word that sounded funny. So Leo said it too!

His mommy's face looked very surprised and sad. "Where did you learn that word?" asked mommy. "That's a bad word that hurts people's feelings."

Leo didn't know! He just thought it sounded funny. But now he understood that some words can make people feel bad.

Mommy explained, "Kind words make people happy. Mean words make people sad. We always want to use kind words."

Leo felt sorry for saying the bad word. He learned to think before speaking. Now Leo uses kind words that make people smile!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Sophie. One day, Sophie saw matches on the table. They looked interesting!

Sophie reached for the matches, but her mommy quickly stopped her. "No! Those are very dangerous!" said mommy.

Mommy sat down with Sophie and explained. "Fire is not a toy. Matches and lighters can start fires that hurt people and burn things."

"If you ever see fire or smoke, you should tell a grown-up right away. And remember: Stop, Drop, and Roll if your clothes catch fire."

Sophie understood now. Fire is very serious. Only grown-ups can use things that make fire. She promised to never touch matches or lighters.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Bella. One day, Bella saw matches on the table. They looked interesting!

Bella reached for the matches, but her daddy quickly stopped her. "No! Those are very dangerous!" said daddy.

Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Ella. For her birthday, Ella got a book from her mommy.

But Ella wasn't happy. "This isn't what I wanted!" she complained. "I wanted something else!" Her mommy looked very sad.

Later, Ella saw a child who had no toys at all. That child looked at Ella's book and said, "Wow, you're so lucky!"

Ella suddenly felt bad for complaining. She realized that having any gift is special. Her mommy worked hard to give her something nice.

Ella ran to her mommy and said, "Thank you for my gift! I love it!" She learned to be grateful for what she has. Being thankful makes everyone happier!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Luna. At school, a bigger kid named Ava was mean to her. Ava called Luna names and made her feel sad.

Luna didn't want to go to school anymore. She would cry and feel scared. But she didn't tell anyone what was happening.

Finally, her dad noticed something was wrong. Luna told them about Ava. Together, they talked to the teacher.

The teacher helped stop the bullying. Ava learned that being mean is wrong. Luna learned that it's important to tell grown-ups when someone is being mean.

Luna felt safe again! She learned that telling someone isn't tattling—it's asking for help. We should always speak up when something is wrong!



Once upon a time, there was a impatient little girl named Flora. Flora loved to play in the basement. One day, her mom reminded her that electrical outlet was dangerous.

Flora said, "Okay, mom!" But she was very curious. When mom wasn't looking, Flora went close to electrical outlet. She thought it would be fun to explore.

But something bad happened. Flora missed the fun. She started to cry and called for her mom. Mom came running and helped her.

Flora felt very sorry. She hugged her mom and said, "I'm sorry I didn't listen." Mom said, "I told you because I love you and want you to be safe."

From that day on, Flora learned that she should always listen to her mom. Some rules are there to keep us safe.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Jasper. After school, Jasper was supposed to do homework. But he wanted to watch TV instead!

Once upon a time, a little girl named Mia and a little boy named Oscar were playing together. They both wanted to use a toy.

"Me first!" yelled Mia. "No, me first!" yelled Oscar. They pushed and pulled, and soon they were both very upset.

An older kid saw them fighting and came over. "Why don't you take turns? One person goes, then the other person goes."

Mia went first for a little while, then it was Oscar's turn. They kept switching, and guess what? They both got to play!

Mia and Oscar learned that taking turns is fair. Everyone gets a chance, and no one feels left out. Now they always take turns and never fight!



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Jack. One day, Jack saw an old lady with heavy bags. At first, Jack just wanted to keep playing.

But then Jack thought, "What if that was me? I would want someone to help!" So Jack went over and asked, "Can I help you?"

The person smiled big and said, "Yes, please! That's so kind of you!" Jack helped as best as he could.

When it was done, the person said, "Thank you so much! You are a wonderful helper!" Jack felt so happy inside, happier than when playing alone.

His dad said, "I'm so proud of you for helping!" Jack learned that helping others makes everyone feel good, especially yourself.

They hugged and played together again! Eli learned that saying sorry is hard but important. It makes friendships strong and helps everyone feel better.

Once upon a time, a little girl named Mia wanted to make a sandcastle. She tried and tried, but it was too hard to do alone!

Then Mia's friend Owen came by. "Need help?" asked Owen. At first, Mia said, "No, I can do it myself!"

But after trying more and failing, Mia finally said, "Okay, please help me." Together, they started working.

With two people helping, the job became easy! They finished quickly and had so much fun doing it together. They high-fived and celebrated!

Mia learned that it's okay to ask for help. Working together makes hard things easier and more fun. Two friends are better than one!



Once upon a time, a little boy named Sam went to the pond with his daddy. It was a hot day and the water looked so inviting!

His daddy said, "Wait for me before going in the water." But Sam was too excited. He ran and jumped right in!

The water was deeper than Sam thought! He couldn't touch the bottom and got scared. He started to splash and cry for help.

His daddy quickly jumped in and pulled Sam out. They were both very shaken up.

Sam learned an important lesson that day. Water can be dangerous! Always wait for a grown-up, and never swim alone. Now Sam always asks for permission before going near water.

Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Maya who had a little bunny named Teddy. Maya loved Teddy very much.

One day, Maya was supposed to give Teddy food and water. But Maya was busy playing with toys and said, "I'll do it later!"

Later came and went, but Maya forgot all about Teddy. The little bunny got very hungry and thirsty. Teddy made sad little sounds.

Maya's mom said, "Did you feed Teddy?" Maya suddenly remembered and felt very bad. She ran to feed and give water to the bunny.

"Teddy depends on you," said her parent. "Pets need us to take care of them." Maya promised to always remember to care for Teddy first, because pets are family too.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Lydia who had a brother named Charlie. One day, they both wanted the TV remote.

"It's mine!" yelled Lydia. "No, it's mine!" yelled Charlie. They started pushing and grabbing. Soon they were really fighting!

Dad heard the noise and came in. "Stop!" said dad. "Fighting is not okay!" Both Lydia and Charlie were in trouble.

They had to sit in time-out and think about what they did. Dad said, "Use your words, not your hands. Talk about problems."

Lydia and Charlie said sorry to each other. They learned to take turns and talk instead of fight. Using words is much better than fighting!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Stella. Stella only wanted to eat chips. "I don't like vegetables!" she would say every day.

Her dad tried to give Stella healthy food, but Stella always said no. She only ate chips for days and days.

Soon, Stella didn't feel good. Her tummy hurt and she had no energy to play. The doctor said Stella needed to eat healthy food to feel better.

Stella tried the vegetables, just a tiny bite. Hey, it wasn't so bad! Actually, it was pretty good! She tried more healthy foods and started feeling much better.

Now Stella eats lots of good food that makes her strong. She still has treats sometimes, but she knows healthy food is important!

Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Jasper. Jasper had a friend named Violet. They promised to have a tea party the next day.

But when the next day came, Jasper decided to do something else instead. He forgot all about the promise to Violet.

Violet waited and waited, but Jasper never came. Violet felt very sad and disappointed. When Jasper saw Violet later, Violet was crying.

"You promised!" said Violet. Jasper suddenly remembered and felt terrible. "I'm so sorry," said Jasper. "I forgot."

Jasper learned that promises are very important. When we break a promise, we hurt our friends. From then on, Jasper always kept his promises.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Anna. Every morning, Anna didn't want to get up. She played and dawdled instead of getting ready.

One day, because Anna was so slow, she missed the school bus! Her dad had to drive her, and they were both late.

At school, Anna had missed story time, the best part of the day! She was so sad. Her friends had all the fun without her.

That night, her dad helped make a list: wake up, brush teeth, get dressed, eat breakfast. Anna put stickers on the list when she finished each thing.

The next day, Anna got ready quickly! She caught the bus and didn't miss anything. Having a routine makes mornings easier and better!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Stella. Stella had a brother named Max. One day, Max got a pretty dress as a present.

Stella felt jealous. "Why did Max get something and I didn't?" she thought. Stella got so angry that she took the pretty dress and hid it!

Max couldn't find his new thing and started to cry. Dad asked, "Stella, do you know where it is?"

Stella felt bad seeing Max so sad. She went and got the pretty dress and said, "I'm sorry. I took it because I was jealous."

Dad explained, "Everyone gets different things at different times. Max's special day will be your special day another time." Stella hugged Max and learned that jealousy only makes everyone sad.

At first, Sam was too shy to say hello. What if the new kid didn't like him? Sam just watched from far away.

But then Sam thought, "Maybe Stella wants a friend too!" So Sam walked over and said, "Hi! Want to play?"

Stella's face lit up with a big smile. "Yes! I was hoping someone would ask!" They played together and had so much fun!

Sam learned that being brave and saying hello can make new friends. Everyone wants to be included. Now Sam and Stella are best friends!



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Max. For his birthday, Max got a game from his daddy.

But Max wasn't happy. "This isn't what I wanted!" he complained. "I wanted something else!" His daddy looked very sad.

Later, Max saw a child who had no toys at all. That child looked at Max's game and said, "Wow, you're so lucky!"

Max suddenly felt bad for complaining. He realized that having any gift is special. His daddy worked hard to give him something nice.

Max ran to his daddy and said, "Thank you for my gift! I love it!" He learned to be grateful for what he has. Being thankful makes everyone happier!



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Charlie. Every morning, Charlie didn't want to get up. He played and dawdled instead of getting ready.

One day, because Charlie was so slow, he missed the school bus! His mom had to drive him, and they were both late.

At school, Charlie had missed story time, the best part of the day! He was so sad. His friends had all the fun without him.

That night, his mom helped make a list: wake up, brush teeth, get dressed, eat breakfast. Charlie put stickers on the list when he finished each thing.

The next day, Charlie got ready quickly! He caught the bus and didn't miss anything. Having a routine makes mornings easier and better!



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Jack. One day, Jack saw matches on the table. They looked interesting!

Jack reached for the matches, but his dad quickly stopped him. "No! Those are very dangerous!" said dad.

Dad sat down with Jack and explained. "Fire is not a toy. Matches and lighters can start fires that hurt people and burn things."

"If you ever see fire or smoke, you should tell a grown-up right away. And remember: Stop, Drop, and Roll if your clothes catch fire."

Jack understood now. Fire is very serious. Only grown-ups can use things that make fire. He promised to never touch matches or lighters.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Stella who had a brother named Sam. One day, they both wanted a toy.

"It's mine!" yelled Stella. "No, it's mine!" yelled Sam. They started pushing and grabbing. Soon they were really fighting!

Mom heard the noise and came in. "Stop!" said mom. "Fighting is not okay!" Both Stella and Sam were in trouble.

They had to sit in time-out and think about what they did. Mom said, "Use your words, not your hands. Talk about problems."

Stella and Sam said sorry to each other. They learned to take turns and talk instead of fight. Using words is much better than fighting!

"But it looks yummy," said Rose. Mom sat down with Rose to explain something important.

"Medicine helps sick people feel better, but it can make healthy people very sick. Only grown-ups can give medicine, and only when someone needs it."

Charlie's heart was beating fast. He was very scared. "Mommy, I'm sorry," Charlie said with tears in his eyes.

His mommy hugged Charlie tight. "I'm glad you're safe. Some places are dangerous, and that's why we must be careful." Charlie promised to always listen and never wander off again.

"Waiting wasn't so bad!" said Owen with a big smile. He learned that being patient and finding fun things to do makes waiting easier. Good things come to those who wait!

Jasper and Drew learned that taking turns is fair. Everyone gets a chance, and no one feels left out. Now they always take turns and never fight!

Once upon a time, a little girl named Ella went to the mall with her mom. They were having a nice day together.

While her mom was looking at something, a stranger came up to Ella. The stranger smiled and said, "Would you like some candy? Come with me!"

Ella remembered what her mom had taught her. She said loudly, "No! I don't talk to strangers!" Then Ella ran back to her mom.

Ella told her mom what happened. Mom was so proud! "You did the right thing! Never go anywhere with someone you don't know."

Ella felt brave and safe. She learned that it's always okay to say no to strangers and run to a grown-up you trust.

Theo felt safe again! He learned that telling someone isn't tattling—it's asking for help. We should always speak up when something is wrong!

Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Pearl. Pearl only wanted to eat chips. "I don't like carrots!" she would say every day.

Her dad tried to give Pearl healthy food, but Pearl always said no. She only ate chips for days and days.

Soon, Pearl didn't feel good. Her tummy hurt and she had no energy to play. The doctor said Pearl needed to eat healthy food to feel better.

Pearl tried the carrots, just a tiny bite. Hey, it wasn't so bad! Actually, it was pretty good! She tried more healthy foods and started feeling much better.

Now Pearl eats lots of good food that makes her strong. She still has treats sometimes, but she knows healthy food is important!



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Jake. For his birthday, Jake got a game from his daddy.

But Jake wasn't happy. "This isn't what I wanted!" he complained. "I wanted something else!" His daddy looked very sad.

Later, Jake saw a child who had no toys at all. That child looked at Jake's game and said, "Wow, you're so lucky!"

Jake suddenly felt bad for complaining. He realized that having any gift is special. His daddy worked hard to give him something nice.

Jake ran to his daddy and said, "Thank you for my gift! I love it!" He learned to be grateful for what he has. Being thankful makes everyone happier!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Olive. Olive didn't like to listen to rules. She thought rules were boring!

One day, Olive's daddy said not to do something. But Olive didn't listen. She kept running away from parents at the store anyway.

Then something bad happened. Olive got lost for a very long time. She wished she had listened!

Olive's daddy wasn't angry, just sad. "I told you because I love you and want to keep you safe," daddy said.

Olive finally understood. Rules aren't to be mean—they're to protect us! She learned that lesson the hard way. Now she listens more carefully.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Ethan. One day at school, Ethan saw a new little girl named Olive.

At first, Ethan was too shy to say hello. What if the new kid didn't like him? Ethan just watched from far away.

But then Ethan thought, "Maybe Olive wants a friend too!" So Ethan walked over and said, "Hi! Want to play?"

Olive's face lit up with a big smile. "Yes! I was hoping someone would ask!" They played together and had so much fun!

Ethan learned that being brave and saying hello can make new friends. Everyone wants to be included. Now Ethan and Olive are best friends!



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Charlie. Charlie didn't like to listen to rules. He thought rules were boring!

One day, Charlie's dad said not to do something. But Charlie didn't listen. He kept playing too close to the road anyway.

Then something bad happened. Charlie almost got hit by a car and was very scared. He wished he had listened!

Charlie's dad wasn't angry, just sad. "I told you because I love you and want to keep you safe," dad said.

Charlie finally understood. Rules aren't to be mean—they're to protect us! He learned that lesson the hard way. Now he listens more carefully.



Once upon a time, a little girl named Leah loved going to the playground. Her favorite thing was the slide.

One day, Leah wanted to show off. She climbed higher than she should and hung upside down in a silly way. "Look at me!" she yelled.

But then Leah lost her grip and fell! She hurt her arm and started to cry. Her dad came running.

At the doctor, they said Leah's arm would be okay, but she had to wear a bandage and rest. Leah couldn't play for a whole week!

Leah learned that playground rules are there to keep us safe. Showing off and being silly on equipment can lead to getting hurt. Play safe, have fun!



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Felix. One day, Felix saw a friend who lost a toy. At first, Felix just wanted to keep playing.

But then Felix thought, "What if that was me? I would want someone to help!" So Felix went over and asked, "Can I help you?"

The person smiled big and said, "Yes, please! That's so kind of you!" Felix helped as best as he could.

When it was done, the person said, "Thank you so much! You are a wonderful helper!" Felix felt so happy inside, happier than when playing alone.

His dad said, "I'm so proud of you for helping!" Felix learned that helping others makes everyone feel good, especially yourself.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Cole. Cole was afraid of trying new things. Whenever he saw trying new things, he would hide!

One day, his mom said, "Let's try to be brave together." Cole was nervous but held his mom's hand tight.

They faced trying new things slowly and carefully. At first, Cole was still scared. But his mom was right there.

Little by little, Cole felt less afraid. He realized that with help, trying new things wasn't so scary after all!

Cole was so proud of being brave! He learned that it's okay to be afraid, but facing your fears makes you stronger. And having someone to help makes it easier.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Theo. Theo was very excited about birthday cake. But his mommy said he had to wait.

"I don't want to wait! I want it now!" said Theo. He started to stomp his feet and whine.

But being impatient didn't help. It just made Theo feel worse. his mommy said, "Being upset won't make time go faster."

Theo tried to be patient. He played with toys and helped his mommy. Before Theo knew it, it was time!

"Waiting wasn't so bad!" said Theo with a big smile. He learned that being patient and finding fun things to do makes waiting easier. Good things come to those who wait!

They faced the dark slowly and carefully. At first, Milo was still scared. But his daddy was right there.

Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Sam. One day at the park, Sam saw a new little girl named Lydia.

At first, Sam was too shy to say hello. What if the new kid didn't like him? Sam just watched from far away.

But then Sam thought, "Maybe Lydia wants a friend too!" So Sam walked over and said, "Hi! Want to play?"

Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Luke. Luke was very excited about a yummy treat. But his daddy said he had to wait.

"I don't want to wait! I want it now!" said Luke. He started to stomp his feet and whine.

Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Bella. At school, a bigger kid named Hugo was mean to her. Hugo called Bella names and made her feel sad.

Bella didn't want to go to school anymore. She would cry and feel scared. But she didn't tell anyone what was happening.

Finally, her mom noticed something was wrong. Bella told them about Hugo. Together, they talked to the teacher.

The teacher helped stop the bullying. Hugo learned that being mean is wrong. Bella learned that it's important to tell grown-ups when someone is being mean.

Bella felt safe again! She learned that telling someone isn't tattling—it's asking for help. We should always speak up when something is wrong!



Once upon a time, a little girl named Ruby went to the beach with her grandma. Ruby loved exploring and seeing all the plants and animals.

While walking, Ruby saw a snake. It looked so cool! Ruby wanted to touch it and take it home.

But her grandma said, "Wait! We should only look, not touch. Some things in nature can be dangerous or need to stay where they are."

Grandma explained that touching the wrong things could hurt Ruby or the animals. "We're just visitors here. We should respect nature."

Ruby understood. She took pictures with her eyes instead of her hands. Looking is wonderful too! Ruby learned to enjoy nature safely and respectfully.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Nora who had a special train set. It was her favorite toy in the whole world!

But Nora didn't take good care of it. She left it outside in the rain, threw it around, and never put it away nicely.

One day, the train set broke! A piece fell off and it didn't work anymore. Nora was so sad and cried. She wanted her favorite toy back!

Her daddy said, "If you had taken better care of it, it might not have broken. Things need love and care."

Nora learned to take care of her things. She puts toys away nicely now and treats them gently. Taking care of our things makes them last longer!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Anna. One day, Anna really wanted to skip bath time. But her daddy said no.

Anna got very angry! She started to scream and cry and kick her feet. She threw a big tantrum right there!

But the tantrum didn't work. her daddy waited until Anna calmed down. "Screaming won't change my answer," said daddy.

Anna was tired from all the crying. She felt silly. The tantrum didn't get her what she wanted. It just made her tired and sad.

Anna learned that throwing tantrums doesn't help. It's better to use words and accept when the answer is no. Sometimes grown-ups know what's best.



Once upon a time, a reckless little girl named Bella went to the meadow with her dad. Bella loved to explore and discover new things.

While walking, Bella saw a frozen lake. It looked exciting! She forgot what her dad said about staying close. Bella ran toward it to take a closer look.

"Stop!" yelled her dad. But Bella got too close and almost fell in! Her dad grabbed her just in time.

Bella's heart was beating fast. She was very scared. "Dad, I'm sorry," Bella said with tears in her eyes.

Her dad hugged Bella tight. "I'm glad you're safe. Some places are dangerous, and that's why we must be careful." Bella promised to always listen and never wander off again.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Tommy. Tommy never liked to clean up. His room was always very messy!

One day, Tommy couldn't find his pet hamster. He looked everywhere but there was so much stuff on the floor! Tommy started to cry.

His mommy said, "If you kept your room clean, you could find your things." Tommy knew mommy was right.

Together, they cleaned the whole room. They picked up toys, folded clothes, and put things in their place. And guess what? They found the pet hamster!

Tommy was so happy! He learned that keeping things clean helps you find what you need. A tidy room is a happy room!

Once upon a time, a little girl named Luna went to the store with her grandma. There were so many exciting things to see!

Luna saw something shiny and colorful. Without thinking, she walked toward it, leaving her grandma behind. Luna walked and walked until...

She looked around and didn't see her grandma anywhere! Luna was lost! She felt very scared and started to cry.

A kind worker found Luna and helped find her grandma. When they were together again, Luna hugged her grandma so tight!

"Never wander off without me," said grandma. Luna learned to always stay close to her grandma in busy places. It's scary to be lost.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Nina who had a little kitten named Max. Nina loved Max very much.

One day, Nina was supposed to give Max food and water. But Nina was busy playing with toys and said, "I'll do it later!"

Later came and went, but Nina forgot all about Max. The little kitten got very hungry and thirsty. Max made sad little sounds.

Nina's dad said, "Did you feed Max?" Nina suddenly remembered and felt very bad. She ran to feed and give water to the kitten.

"Max depends on you," said her parent. "Pets need us to take care of them." Nina promised to always remember to care for Max first, because pets are family too.

Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Ruby. Ruby never wanted to go to bed. "I'm not tired!" she always said.

One night, Ruby stayed up very, very late playing with toys. Her mommy said, "Time for bed!" But Ruby hid under the covers and kept playing.

The next day, Ruby was so tired! She couldn't run. She couldn't play. She fell asleep at breakfast!

Her mommy said, "This is why we need sleep. Our bodies need rest to play and have fun."

That night, Ruby went to bed on time. The next day, she had so much energy! Ruby learned that sleep helps us feel good and have fun. Now bedtime isn't so bad!

Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Jasper. One day, Jasper didn't share to his friend Leo. Leo was very sad.

At first, Jasper didn't want to say sorry. He felt embarrassed and a little stubborn. But Leo wouldn't play with him anymore.

Jasper's dad said, "When we hurt someone, we need to say sorry. It helps fix the hurt."

Jasper found Leo and said, "I'm really sorry for what I did. It was wrong. Can you forgive me?" Leo smiled and said yes.

They hugged and played together again! Jasper learned that saying sorry is hard but important. It makes friendships strong and helps everyone feel better.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Drew. Drew was always in a hurry. He never wanted to slow down!

One day, his daddy said, "Be careful! Don't go so fast!" But Drew didn't listen. He was riding a bike too fast, going faster and faster.

Suddenly, Drew tripped and fell! He scraped his knee and it hurt a lot. Drew started to cry.

His daddy came and put a bandage on the scrape. "This is why I asked you to slow down," said daddy gently.

Drew's knee hurt for several days. He learned that rushing can lead to accidents. It's better to slow down and be careful than to get hurt.

Once upon a time, a little girl named Zoe and a little boy named Adam were playing together. They both wanted to use the bike.

"Me first!" yelled Zoe. "No, me first!" yelled Adam. They pushed and pulled, and soon they were both very upset.

An older kid saw them fighting and came over. "Why don't you take turns? One person goes, then the other person goes."

Zoe went first for a little while, then it was Adam's turn. They kept switching, and guess what? They both got to play!

Zoe and Adam learned that taking turns is fair. Everyone gets a chance, and no one feels left out. Now they always take turns and never fight!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Hazel. One day, Hazel heard some big kids say a word that sounded funny. So Hazel said it too!

Her daddy's face looked very surprised and sad. "Where did you learn that word?" asked daddy. "That's a bad word that hurts people's feelings."

Hazel didn't know! She just thought it sounded funny. But now she understood that some words can make people feel bad.

Daddy explained, "Kind words make people happy. Mean words make people sad. We always want to use kind words."

Hazel felt sorry for saying the bad word. She learned to think before speaking. Now Hazel uses kind words that make people smile!

Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Nora. One day, Nora saw a bottle on the counter. It looked like candy!

Nora reached for it, but her daddy quickly took it away. "No! That's medicine, not candy!" said daddy.

"But it looks yummy," said Nora. Daddy sat down with Nora to explain something important.

"Medicine helps sick people feel better, but it can make healthy people very sick. Only grown-ups can give medicine, and only when someone needs it."

Nora understood now. Medicine is not a treat. She promised to never touch medicine bottles. Some things that look like candy can be dangerous!

Once upon a time, a little boy named Liam went to the market with his grandpa. There were so many exciting things to see!

Liam saw something shiny and colorful. Without thinking, he walked toward it, leaving his grandpa behind. Liam walked and walked until...

He looked around and didn't see his grandpa anywhere! Liam was lost! He felt very scared and started to cry.

A kind worker found Liam and helped find his grandpa. When they were together again, Liam hugged his grandpa so tight!

"Never wander off without me," said grandpa. Liam learned to always stay close to his grandpa in busy places. It's scary to be lost.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Nora who had a special doll. It was her favorite toy in the whole world!

But Nora didn't take good care of it. She left it outside in the rain, threw it around, and never put it away nicely.

One day, the doll broke! A piece fell off and it didn't work anymore. Nora was so sad and cried. She wanted her favorite toy back!

Her mom said, "If you had taken better care of it, it might not have broken. Things need love and care."

Nora learned to take care of her things. She puts toys away nicely now and treats them gently. Taking care of our things makes them last longer!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Chloe. Chloe had a favorite blocks that she loved very much. She played with it every day.

One day, her little brother Noah came and asked, "Can I play with your blocks?" But Chloe said, "No! It's mine! Go away!"

Noah was very sad and started to cry. Chloe kept playing alone, but it didn't feel fun anymore. She saw how sad Noah was and felt bad inside.

Finally, Chloe went to Noah and said, "I'm sorry. We can play together." Noah's face lit up with a big smile. They played with the blocks together and had so much more fun!

Chloe learned that sharing makes everyone happy. When we share, we make more friends and have more fun.



Once upon a time, a little boy named Adam went to the mall with his grandma. They were having a nice day together.

While his grandma was looking at something, a stranger came up to Adam. The stranger smiled and said, "Would you like some candy? Come with me!"

Adam remembered what his grandma had taught him. He said loudly, "No! I don't talk to strangers!" Then Adam ran back to his grandma.

Adam told his grandma what happened. Grandma was so proud! "You did the right thing! Never go anywhere with someone you don't know."

Adam felt brave and safe. He learned that it's always okay to say no to strangers and run to a grown-up you trust.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Maya. Maya had a brother named Liam. One day, Liam got a new toy as a present.

Maya felt bad seeing Liam so sad. She went and got the new toy and said, "I'm sorry. I took it because I was jealous."

Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Tim. One day, Tim saw matches on the table. They looked interesting!

Tim reached for the matches, but his daddy quickly stopped him. "No! Those are very dangerous!" said daddy.

Daddy sat down with Tim and explained. "Fire is not a toy. Matches and lighters can start fires that hurt people and burn things."

"If you ever see fire or smoke, you should tell a grown-up right away. And remember: Stop, Drop, and Roll if your clothes catch fire."

Tim understood now. Fire is very serious. Only grown-ups can use things that make fire. He promised to never touch matches or lighters.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Hazel. Every morning, Hazel didn't want to get up. She played and dawdled instead of getting ready.

One day, because Hazel was so slow, she missed the school bus! Her mommy had to drive her, and they were both late.

At school, Hazel had missed story time, the best part of the day! She was so sad. Her friends had all the fun without her.

That night, her mommy helped make a list: wake up, brush teeth, get dressed, eat breakfast. Hazel put stickers on the list when she finished each thing.

The next day, Hazel got ready quickly! She caught the bus and didn't miss anything. Having a routine makes mornings easier and better!



Once upon a time, a little girl named Lydia went to the beach with her dad. Lydia loved exploring and seeing all the plants and animals.

While walking, Lydia saw a bird's nest. It looked so cool! Lydia wanted to touch it and take it home.

But her dad said, "Wait! We should only look, not touch. Some things in nature can be dangerous or need to stay where they are."

Dad explained that touching the wrong things could hurt Lydia or the animals. "We're just visitors here. We should respect nature."

Lydia understood. She took pictures with her eyes instead of her hands. Looking is wonderful too! Lydia learned to enjoy nature safely and respectfully.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Milo. One day, Milo heard some big kids say a word that sounded funny. So Milo said it too!

His mom's face looked very surprised and sad. "Where did you learn that word?" asked mom. "That's a bad word that hurts people's feelings."

Milo didn't know! He just thought it sounded funny. But now he understood that some words can make people feel bad.

Mom explained, "Kind words make people happy. Mean words make people sad. We always want to use kind words."

Milo felt sorry for saying the bad word. He learned to think before speaking. Now Milo uses kind words that make people smile!

Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Felix. Felix loved watching cartoons on the TV. He watched for hours and hours every day.

His mommy said, "You watch too much TV. Go play outside!" But Felix didn't want to stop.

After many days of too much TV, Felix's head started to hurt. His eyes felt tired. He didn't feel good at all.

The doctor said Felix needed to rest his eyes and play more. So Felix went outside and discovered how fun it was to run and play!

Felix learned that too much TV isn't good for you. Playing outside and using your imagination is much more fun. Now Felix only watches a little TV each day.

Eli and Sam learned that taking turns is fair. Everyone gets a chance, and no one feels left out. Now they always take turns and never fight!

Archie was very scared. When mom came and asked what happened, Archie said, "I didn't do it! Maybe the wind did it!" But there was no wind inside the house.

Mom looked at Archie with sad eyes. "Are you telling me the truth?" Archie looked at the floor and didn't say anything. He felt bad for lying.

Finally, Archie said, "I'm sorry, mom. I did it. I was playing too rough and it was an accident. I was scared to tell you."

Mom hugged Archie and said, "Thank you for telling the truth. Accidents happen, and I'm not angry. But lying makes things worse. Always tell the truth, even when you're scared." Archie felt much better after being honest.

One day, the toy plane broke! A piece fell off and it didn't work anymore. Oscar was so sad and cried. He wanted his favorite toy back!

His dad said, "If you had taken better care of it, it might not have broken. Things need love and care."

Oscar learned to take care of his things. He puts toys away nicely now and treats them gently. Taking care of our things makes them last longer!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Mia. Mia loved watching cartoons on the TV. She watched for hours and hours every day.

Her mom said, "You watch too much TV. Go play outside!" But Mia didn't want to stop.

After many days of too much TV, Mia's head started to hurt. Her eyes felt tired. She didn't feel good at all.

The doctor said Mia needed to rest her eyes and play more. So Mia went outside and discovered how fun it was to run and play!

Mia learned that too much TV isn't good for you. Playing outside and using your imagination is much more fun. Now Mia only watches a little TV each day.



Once upon a time, a little girl named Nora and a little girl named Nina were playing together. They both wanted to use the ball.

"Me first!" yelled Nora. "No, me first!" yelled Nina. They pushed and pulled, and soon they were both very upset.

An older kid saw them fighting and came over. "Why don't you take turns? One person goes, then the other person goes."

Nora went first for a little while, then it was Nina's turn. They kept switching, and guess what? They both got to play!

Nora and Nina learned that taking turns is fair. Everyone gets a chance, and no one feels left out. Now they always take turns and never fight!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Olive. Olive was very excited about to go to the park. But her mommy said she had to wait.

"I don't want to wait! I want it now!" said Olive. She started to stomp her feet and whine.

But being impatient didn't help. It just made Olive feel worse. her mommy said, "Being upset won't make time go faster."

Olive tried to be patient. She played with toys and helped her mommy. Before Olive knew it, it was time!

"Waiting wasn't so bad!" said Olive with a big smile. She learned that being patient and finding fun things to do makes waiting easier. Good things come to those who wait!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Violet who had a little bunny named Cookie. Violet loved Cookie very much.

One day, Violet was supposed to give Cookie food and water. But Violet was busy playing with toys and said, "I'll do it later!"

Later came and went, but Violet forgot all about Cookie. The little bunny got very hungry and thirsty. Cookie made sad little sounds.

Violet's mom said, "Did you feed Cookie?" Violet suddenly remembered and felt very bad. She ran to feed and give water to the bunny.

"Cookie depends on you," said her parent. "Pets need us to take care of them." Violet promised to always remember to care for Cookie first, because pets are family too.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Zach. Zach only wanted to eat cake. "I don't like vegetables!" he would say every day.

His daddy tried to give Zach healthy food, but Zach always said no. He only ate cake for days and days.

Soon, Zach didn't feel good. His tummy hurt and he had no energy to play. The doctor said Zach needed to eat healthy food to feel better.

Zach tried the vegetables, just a tiny bite. Hey, it wasn't so bad! Actually, it was pretty good! He tried more healthy foods and started feeling much better.

Now Zach eats lots of good food that makes him strong. He still has treats sometimes, but he knows healthy food is important!



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Drew. Drew only wanted to eat cake. "I don't like fruits!" he would say every day.

His daddy tried to give Drew healthy food, but Drew always said no. He only ate cake for days and days.

Soon, Drew didn't feel good. His tummy hurt and he had no energy to play. The doctor said Drew needed to eat healthy food to feel better.

Now Drew eats lots of good food that makes him strong. He still has treats sometimes, but he knows healthy food is important!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Sara. One day, while playing in the garage, Sara accidentally knocked over mom's pretty bowl. It fell to the floor and broke!

Sara was very scared. When mommy came and asked what happened, Sara said, "I didn't do it! Maybe the wind did it!" But there was no wind inside the house.

Mommy looked at Sara with sad eyes. "Are you telling me the truth?" Sara looked at the floor and didn't say anything. She felt bad for lying.

Finally, Sara said, "I'm sorry, mommy. I did it. I was playing too rough and it was an accident. I was scared to tell you."

Mommy hugged Sara and said, "Thank you for telling the truth. Accidents happen, and I'm not angry. But lying makes things worse. Always tell the truth, even when you're scared." Sara felt much better after being honest.



Once upon a time, a little boy named Owen went to the mall with his dad. They were having a nice day together.

While his dad was looking at something, a stranger came up to Owen. The stranger smiled and said, "Would you like some candy? Come with me!"

Owen remembered what his dad had taught him. He said loudly, "No! I don't talk to strangers!" Then Owen ran back to his dad.

Owen told his dad what happened. Dad was so proud! "You did the right thing! Never go anywhere with someone you don't know."

Owen felt brave and safe. He learned that it's always okay to say no to strangers and run to a grown-up you trust.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Lucy. After school, Lucy was supposed to do homework. But she wanted to play outside instead!

"I'll do it later!" said Lucy, running off to play. Her mommy called, "Remember your homework!" But Lucy didn't listen.

Later came and went. Before Lucy knew it, it was bedtime! She hadn't done any homework. Now it was too late, and she was very tired.

The next day at school, the teacher was disappointed that Lucy didn't have her homework. Lucy felt embarrassed and sad.

After that, Lucy learned to do homework first, then play. When you finish your work first, you can play without worrying! Work first, then play—that's the best way!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Clara who had a special jump rope. It was her favorite toy in the whole world!

But Clara didn't take good care of it. She left it outside in the rain, threw it around, and never put it away nicely.

One day, the jump rope broke! A piece fell off and it didn't work anymore. Clara was so sad and cried. She wanted her favorite toy back!

Her mom said, "If you had taken better care of it, it might not have broken. Things need love and care."

Clara learned to take care of her things. She puts toys away nicely now and treats them gently. Taking care of our things makes them last longer!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Lucy. One day, her mom made delicious milk for Lucy and her little brother Cole.

Mom put the milk on the table. "Make sure you share nicely," said mom. But Lucy wanted all the milk for herself!

When Cole wasn't looking, Lucy took most of the milk. She ate and ate until her tummy hurt very much!

Lucy felt sick and couldn't play anymore. Cole was sad because there wasn't enough milk left. Mom came and saw what happened.

"Being greedy doesn't make you happy," said mom. "Now you don't feel good, and Cole is sad." Lucy said sorry to Cole and learned that being greedy only makes everyone feel bad.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Anna who had a brother named Owen. One day, they both wanted the last cookie.

"It's mine!" yelled Anna. "No, it's mine!" yelled Owen. They started pushing and grabbing. Soon they were really fighting!

Mom heard the noise and came in. "Stop!" said mom. "Fighting is not okay!" Both Anna and Owen were in trouble.

They had to sit in time-out and think about what they did. Mom said, "Use your words, not your hands. Talk about problems."

Anna and Owen said sorry to each other. They learned to take turns and talk instead of fight. Using words is much better than fighting!



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Cole. One day, Cole saw a bottle on the counter. It looked like candy!

Cole reached for it, but his dad quickly took it away. "No! That's medicine, not candy!" said dad.

"But it looks yummy," said Cole. Dad sat down with Cole to explain something important.

"Medicine helps sick people feel better, but it can make healthy people very sick. Only grown-ups can give medicine, and only when someone needs it."

Cole understood now. Medicine is not a treat. He promised to never touch medicine bottles. Some things that look like candy can be dangerous!



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Zach. At school, a bigger kid named Anna was mean to him. Anna called Zach names and made him feel sad.

Zach didn't want to go to school anymore. He would cry and feel scared. But he didn't tell anyone what was happening.

Finally, his dad noticed something was wrong. Zach told them about Anna. Together, they talked to the teacher.

The teacher helped stop the bullying. Anna learned that being mean is wrong. Zach learned that it's important to tell grown-ups when someone is being mean.

Zach felt safe again! He learned that telling someone isn't tattling—it's asking for help. We should always speak up when something is wrong!



Once upon a time, a little boy named Tim went to the zoo with his grandma. There were so many exciting things to see!

Tim saw something shiny and colorful. Without thinking, he walked toward it, leaving his grandma behind. Tim walked and walked until...

He looked around and didn't see his grandma anywhere! Tim was lost! He felt very scared and started to cry.

A kind worker found Tim and helped find his grandma. When they were together again, Tim hugged his grandma so tight!

"Never wander off without me," said grandma. Tim learned to always stay close to his grandma in busy places. It's scary to be lost.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Milo. One day, Milo really wanted a new game. But his mommy said no.

Milo got very angry! He started to scream and cry and kick his feet. He threw a big tantrum right there!

But the tantrum didn't work. his mommy waited until Milo calmed down. "Screaming won't change my answer," said mommy.

Milo was tired from all the crying. He felt silly. The tantrum didn't get him what he wanted. It just made him tired and sad.

Milo learned that throwing tantrums doesn't help. It's better to use words and accept when the answer is no. Sometimes grown-ups know what's best.

Once upon a time, a little boy named Eli wanted to finish a big puzzle. He tried and tried, but it was too hard to do alone!

Then Eli's friend Archie came by. "Need help?" asked Archie. At first, Eli said, "No, I can do it myself!"

But after trying more and failing, Eli finally said, "Okay, please help me." Together, they started working.

With two people helping, the job became easy! They finished quickly and had so much fun doing it together. They high-fived and celebrated!

Eli learned that it's okay to ask for help. Working together makes hard things easier and more fun. Two friends are better than one!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Clara. Clara was afraid of thunder. Whenever she saw thunder, she would hide!

One day, her dad said, "Let's try to be brave together." Clara was nervous but held her dad's hand tight.

They faced thunder slowly and carefully. At first, Clara was still scared. But her dad was right there.

Little by little, Clara felt less afraid. She realized that with help, thunder wasn't so scary after all!

Clara was so proud of being brave! She learned that it's okay to be afraid, but facing your fears makes you stronger. And having someone to help makes it easier.

Later, Liam saw a child who had no toys at all. That child looked at Liam's art supplies and said, "Wow, you're so lucky!"

Liam ran to his daddy and said, "Thank you for my gift! I love it!" He learned to be grateful for what he has. Being thankful makes everyone happier!

Ava felt better after a hug and a kiss. But she learned an important lesson: the rules are there to keep her safe.

From then on, Ava remembered to be more careful. Getting hurt is no fun, and following the rules helps avoid accidents!

Once upon a time, a little girl named Ella went to the park with her grandpa. Ella loved exploring and seeing all the plants and animals.

While walking, Ella saw flowers. It looked so cool! Ella wanted to touch it and take it home.

But her grandpa said, "Wait! We should only look, not touch. Some things in nature can be dangerous or need to stay where they are."

Grandpa explained that touching the wrong things could hurt Ella or the animals. "We're just visitors here. We should respect nature."

Ella understood. She took pictures with her eyes instead of her hands. Looking is wonderful too! Ella learned to enjoy nature safely and respectfully.

Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Noah. One day, Noah saw matches on the table. They looked interesting!

Noah reached for the matches, but his mom quickly stopped him. "No! Those are very dangerous!" said mom.

Mom sat down with Noah and explained. "Fire is not a toy. Matches and lighters can start fires that hurt people and burn things."

"If you ever see fire or smoke, you should tell a grown-up right away. And remember: Stop, Drop, and Roll if your clothes catch fire."

Noah understood now. Fire is very serious. Only grown-ups can use things that make fire. He promised to never touch matches or lighters.

The next day, Max got ready quickly! He caught the bus and didn't miss anything. Having a routine makes mornings easier and better!

Once upon a time, a little boy named Liam went to the park with his grandpa. They were having a nice day together.

While his grandpa was looking at something, a stranger came up to Liam. The stranger smiled and said, "Would you like some candy? Come with me!"

Liam remembered what his grandpa had taught him. He said loudly, "No! I don't talk to strangers!" Then Liam ran back to his grandpa.

Liam told his grandpa what happened. Grandpa was so proud! "You did the right thing! Never go anywhere with someone you don't know."

Liam felt brave and safe. He learned that it's always okay to say no to strangers and run to a grown-up you trust.



Once upon a time, a little boy named Charlie went to the beach with his grandma. Charlie loved exploring and seeing all the plants and animals.

While walking, Charlie saw mushrooms. It looked so cool! Charlie wanted to touch it and take it home.

But his grandma said, "Wait! We should only look, not touch. Some things in nature can be dangerous or need to stay where they are."

Grandma explained that touching the wrong things could hurt Charlie or the animals. "We're just visitors here. We should respect nature."

Charlie understood. He took pictures with his eyes instead of his hands. Looking is wonderful too! Charlie learned to enjoy nature safely and respectfully.



Once upon a time, a little boy named Max wanted to carry heavy boxes. He tried and tried, but it was too hard to do alone!

Then Max's friend Rose came by. "Need help?" asked Rose. At first, Max said, "No, I can do it myself!"

But after trying more and failing, Max finally said, "Okay, please help me." Together, they started working.

With two people helping, the job became easy! They finished quickly and had so much fun doing it together. They high-fived and celebrated!

Max learned that it's okay to ask for help. Working together makes hard things easier and more fun. Two friends are better than one!



Once upon a time, a little boy named Ethan went to the forest with his dad. Ethan loved exploring and seeing all the plants and animals.

While walking, Ethan saw a bee hive. It looked so cool! Ethan wanted to touch it and take it home.

But his dad said, "Wait! We should only look, not touch. Some things in nature can be dangerous or need to stay where they are."

Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Ben. After school, Ben was supposed to do homework. But he wanted to play with toys instead!

"I'll do it later!" said Ben, running off to play. His dad called, "Remember your homework!" But Ben didn't listen.

Later came and went. Before Ben knew it, it was bedtime! He hadn't done any homework. Now it was too late, and he was very tired.

The next day at school, the teacher was disappointed that Ben didn't have his homework. Ben felt embarrassed and sad.

After that, Ben learned to do homework first, then play. When you finish your work first, you can play without worrying! Work first, then play—that's the best way!



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Jasper. One day, Jasper really wanted more candy. But his mom said no.

Jasper got very angry! He started to scream and cry and kick his feet. He threw a big tantrum right there!

But the tantrum didn't work. his mom waited until Jasper calmed down. "Screaming won't change my answer," said mom.

Jasper was tired from all the crying. He felt silly. The tantrum didn't get him what he wanted. It just made him tired and sad.

Jasper learned that throwing tantrums doesn't help. It's better to use words and accept when the answer is no. Sometimes grown-ups know what's best.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Lucy. Lucy had a favorite kite that she loved very much. She played with it every day.

Luke was very sad and started to cry. Lucy kept playing alone, but it didn't feel fun anymore. She saw how sad Luke was and felt bad inside.

Finally, Lucy went to Luke and said, "I'm sorry. We can play together." Luke's face lit up with a big smile. They played with the kite together and had so much more fun!

Lucy learned that sharing makes everyone happy. When we share, we make more friends and have more fun.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Oscar who had a sister named Maya. One day, they both wanted a book.

"It's mine!" yelled Oscar. "No, it's mine!" yelled Maya. They started pushing and grabbing. Soon they were really fighting!

Mom heard the noise and came in. "Stop!" said mom. "Fighting is not okay!" Both Oscar and Maya were in trouble.

They had to sit in time-out and think about what they did. Mom said, "Use your words, not your hands. Talk about problems."

Oscar and Maya said sorry to each other. They learned to take turns and talk instead of fight. Using words is much better than fighting!

His mom said, "This is why we need sleep. Our bodies need rest to play and have fun."

That night, Jack went to bed on time. The next day, he had so much energy! Jack learned that sleep helps us feel good and have fun. Now bedtime isn't so bad!

Clara was very scared. When mom came and asked what happened, Clara said, "I didn't do it! Maybe the wind did it!" But there was no wind inside the house.

Mom looked at Clara with sad eyes. "Are you telling me the truth?" Clara looked at the floor and didn't say anything. She felt bad for lying.

Finally, Clara said, "I'm sorry, mom. I did it. I was playing too rough and it was an accident. I was scared to tell you."

Mom hugged Clara and said, "Thank you for telling the truth. Accidents happen, and I'm not angry. But lying makes things worse. Always tell the truth, even when you're scared." Clara felt much better after being honest.

Oscar tried to be patient. He played with toys and helped his mom. Before Oscar knew it, it was time!

"Waiting wasn't so bad!" said Oscar with a big smile. He learned that being patient and finding fun things to do makes waiting easier. Good things come to those who wait!



Once upon a time, a little girl named Zoe and a little girl named Lydia were playing together. They both wanted to use the swing.

"Me first!" yelled Zoe. "No, me first!" yelled Lydia. They pushed and pulled, and soon they were both very upset.

An older kid saw them fighting and came over. "Why don't you take turns? One person goes, then the other person goes."

Zoe went first for a little while, then it was Lydia's turn. They kept switching, and guess what? They both got to play!

Zoe and Lydia learned that taking turns is fair. Everyone gets a chance, and no one feels left out. Now they always take turns and never fight!



Once upon a time, a cheerful little boy named Ryan went to the meadow with his mommy. Ryan loved to explore and discover new things.

While walking, Ryan saw a dark cave. It looked exciting! He forgot what his mommy said about staying close. Ryan ran toward it to take a closer look.

"Stop!" yelled his mommy. But Ryan got too close and almost fell in! His mommy grabbed him just in time.

Ryan's heart was beating fast. He was very scared. "Mommy, I'm sorry," Ryan said with tears in his eyes.

His mommy hugged Ryan tight. "I'm glad you're safe. Some places are dangerous, and that's why we must be careful." Ryan promised to always listen and never wander off again.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Ryan. Ryan never wanted to go to bed. "I'm not tired!" he always said.

One night, Ryan stayed up very, very late playing with toys. His mom said, "Time for bed!" But Ryan hid under the covers and kept playing.

The next day, Ryan was so tired! He couldn't run. He couldn't play. He fell asleep at breakfast!

His mom said, "This is why we need sleep. Our bodies need rest to play and have fun."

That night, Ryan went to bed on time. The next day, he had so much energy! Ryan learned that sleep helps us feel good and have fun. Now bedtime isn't so bad!



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Eli. Eli never liked to clean up. His room was always very messy!

One day, Eli couldn't find his pet hamster. He looked everywhere but there was so much stuff on the floor! Eli started to cry.

His mommy said, "If you kept your room clean, you could find your things." Eli knew mommy was right.

Together, they cleaned the whole room. They picked up toys, folded clothes, and put things in their place. And guess what? They found the pet hamster!

Eli was so happy! He learned that keeping things clean helps you find what you need. A tidy room is a happy room!



Once upon a time, a little girl named Mia wanted to finish a big puzzle. She tried and tried, but it was too hard to do alone!

Then Mia's friend Violet came by. "Need help?" asked Violet. At first, Mia said, "No, I can do it myself!"

But after trying more and failing, Mia finally said, "Okay, please help me." Together, they started working.

With two people helping, the job became easy! They finished quickly and had so much fun doing it together. They high-fived and celebrated!

Mia learned that it's okay to ask for help. Working together makes hard things easier and more fun. Two friends are better than one!



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Hugo. One day, Hugo saw matches on the table. They looked interesting!

Hugo reached for the matches, but his mom quickly stopped him. "No! Those are very dangerous!" said mom.

Mom sat down with Hugo and explained. "Fire is not a toy. Matches and lighters can start fires that hurt people and burn things."

"If you ever see fire or smoke, you should tell a grown-up right away. And remember: Stop, Drop, and Roll if your clothes catch fire."

Hugo understood now. Fire is very serious. Only grown-ups can use things that make fire. He promised to never touch matches or lighters.



Once upon a time, a little girl named Sara went to the forest with her dad. Sara loved exploring and seeing all the plants and animals.

While walking, Sara saw a wild animal. It looked so cool! Sara wanted to touch it and take it home.

But her dad said, "Wait! We should only look, not touch. Some things in nature can be dangerous or need to stay where they are."

Dad explained that touching the wrong things could hurt Sara or the animals. "We're just visitors here. We should respect nature."

Sara understood. She took pictures with her eyes instead of her hands. Looking is wonderful too! Sara learned to enjoy nature safely and respectfully.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Hazel. Hazel loved watching cartoons on the TV. She watched for hours and hours every day.

Her dad said, "You watch too much TV. Go play outside!" But Hazel didn't want to stop.

After many days of too much TV, Hazel's head started to hurt. Her eyes felt tired. She didn't feel good at all.

The doctor said Hazel needed to rest her eyes and play more. So Hazel went outside and discovered how fun it was to run and play!

Hazel learned that too much TV isn't good for you. Playing outside and using your imagination is much more fun. Now Hazel only watches a little TV each day.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Stella. Stella only wanted to eat candy. "I don't like apples!" she would say every day.

Her daddy tried to give Stella healthy food, but Stella always said no. She only ate candy for days and days.

Soon, Stella didn't feel good. Her tummy hurt and she had no energy to play. The doctor said Stella needed to eat healthy food to feel better.

Stella tried the apples, just a tiny bite. Hey, it wasn't so bad! Actually, it was pretty good! She tried more healthy foods and started feeling much better.

Now Stella eats lots of good food that makes her strong. She still has treats sometimes, but she knows healthy food is important!



Once upon a time, there was a loving little boy named Cole. Cole loved to play in the bedroom. One day, his mommy warned him to stay away from broken glass.

Cole said, "Okay, mommy!" But he was very curious. When mommy wasn't looking, Cole went close to broken glass. He thought it would be fun to explore.

But something bad happened. Cole scared someone. He started to cry and called for his mommy. Mommy came running and helped him.

Cole felt very sorry. He hugged his mommy and said, "I'm sorry I didn't listen." Mommy said, "I told you because I love you and want you to be safe."

From that day on, Cole learned that he should always listen to his mommy. Some rules are there to keep us safe.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Zoe who had a little hamster named Cookie. Zoe loved Cookie very much.

One day, Zoe was supposed to give Cookie food and water. But Zoe was busy playing with toys and said, "I'll do it later!"

Later came and went, but Zoe forgot all about Cookie. The little hamster got very hungry and thirsty. Cookie made sad little sounds.

Zoe's mom said, "Did you feed Cookie?" Zoe suddenly remembered and felt very bad. She ran to feed and give water to the hamster.

"Cookie depends on you," said her parent. "Pets need us to take care of them." Zoe promised to always remember to care for Cookie first, because pets are family too.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Rose. One day, Rose really wanted another cookie. But her mommy said no.

Rose got very angry! She started to scream and cry and kick her feet. She threw a big tantrum right there!

But the tantrum didn't work. her mommy waited until Rose calmed down. "Screaming won't change my answer," said mommy.

Rose was tired from all the crying. She felt silly. The tantrum didn't get her what she wanted. It just made her tired and sad.

Rose learned that throwing tantrums doesn't help. It's better to use words and accept when the answer is no. Sometimes grown-ups know what's best.

Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Eli. Eli had a friend named Mia. They promised to have a picnic the next day.

But when the next day came, Eli decided to do something else instead. He forgot all about the promise to Mia.

Mia waited and waited, but Eli never came. Mia felt very sad and disappointed. When Eli saw Mia later, Mia was crying.

"You promised!" said Mia. Eli suddenly remembered and felt terrible. "I'm so sorry," said Eli. "I forgot."

Eli learned that promises are very important. When we break a promise, we hurt our friends. From then on, Eli always kept his promises.



Once upon a time, a little boy named Tim went to the beach with his dad. It was a hot day and the water looked so inviting!

His dad said, "Wait for me before going in the water." But Tim was too excited. He ran and jumped right in!

The water was deeper than Tim thought! He couldn't touch the bottom and got scared. He started to splash and cry for help.

His dad quickly jumped in and pulled Tim out. They were both very shaken up.

Tim learned an important lesson that day. Water can be dangerous! Always wait for a grown-up, and never swim alone. Now Tim always asks for permission before going near water.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Nina. One day, while playing in the hallway, Nina accidentally knocked over the family photo frame. It fell to the floor and broke!

Nina was very scared. When dad came and asked what happened, Nina said, "I didn't do it! Maybe the wind did it!" But there was no wind inside the house.

Dad looked at Nina with sad eyes. "Are you telling me the truth?" Nina looked at the floor and didn't say anything. She felt bad for lying.

Finally, Nina said, "I'm sorry, dad. I did it. I was playing too rough and it was an accident. I was scared to tell you."

Dad hugged Nina and said, "Thank you for telling the truth. Accidents happen, and I'm not angry. But lying makes things worse. Always tell the truth, even when you're scared." Nina felt much better after being honest.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Cole. One day at the park, Cole saw a new little boy named Ryan.

At first, Cole was too shy to say hello. What if the new kid didn't like him? Cole just watched from far away.

But then Cole thought, "Maybe Ryan wants a friend too!" So Cole walked over and said, "Hi! Want to play?"

Ryan's face lit up with a big smile. "Yes! I was hoping someone would ask!" They played together and had so much fun!

Cole learned that being brave and saying hello can make new friends. Everyone wants to be included. Now Cole and Ryan are best friends!

From then on, Stella remembered to be more careful. Getting hurt is no fun, and following the rules helps avoid accidents!

Henry was so proud of being brave! He learned that it's okay to be afraid, but facing your fears makes you stronger. And having someone to help makes it easier.

Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Emma. Every morning, Emma didn't want to get up. She played and dawdled instead of getting ready.

One day, because Emma was so slow, she missed the school bus! Her daddy had to drive her, and they were both late.

At school, Emma had missed story time, the best part of the day! She was so sad. Her friends had all the fun without her.

That night, her daddy helped make a list: wake up, brush teeth, get dressed, eat breakfast. Emma put stickers on the list when she finished each thing.

The next day, Emma got ready quickly! She caught the bus and didn't miss anything. Having a routine makes mornings easier and better!
