Ruby didn't want to go to school anymore. She would cry and feel scared. But she didn't tell anyone what was happening.

Finally, her mom noticed something was wrong. Ruby told them about Nina. Together, they talked to the teacher.

The teacher helped stop the bullying. Nina learned that being mean is wrong. Ruby learned that it's important to tell grown-ups when someone is being mean.

Ruby felt safe again! She learned that telling someone isn't tattling—it's asking for help. We should always speak up when something is wrong!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Ivy. Ivy was afraid of thunder. Whenever she saw thunder, she would hide!

One day, her daddy said, "Let's try to be brave together." Ivy was nervous but held her daddy's hand tight.

They faced thunder slowly and carefully. At first, Ivy was still scared. But her daddy was right there.

Little by little, Ivy felt less afraid. She realized that with help, thunder wasn't so scary after all!

Ivy was so proud of being brave! She learned that it's okay to be afraid, but facing your fears makes you stronger. And having someone to help makes it easier.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Theo who had a little kitten named Oreo. Theo loved Oreo very much.

One day, Theo was supposed to give Oreo food and water. But Theo was busy playing with toys and said, "I'll do it later!"

Later came and went, but Theo forgot all about Oreo. The little kitten got very hungry and thirsty. Oreo made sad little sounds.

Theo's mom said, "Did you feed Oreo?" Theo suddenly remembered and felt very bad. He ran to feed and give water to the kitten.

"Oreo depends on you," said his parent. "Pets need us to take care of them." Theo promised to always remember to care for Oreo first, because pets are family too.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Chloe. Chloe was playing too rough, even though her daddy said not to.

While playing, Chloe got a scrape! It hurt a lot and Chloe started to cry. Her daddy came running to help.

Daddy cleaned the boo-boo and gave Chloe a bandage. "This is why I said to be careful," daddy explained gently.

Chloe felt better after a hug and a kiss. But she learned an important lesson: the rules are there to keep her safe.

From then on, Chloe remembered to be more careful. Getting hurt is no fun, and following the rules helps avoid accidents!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Lydia. One day, Lydia saw dad in the garden. At first, Lydia just wanted to keep playing.

But then Lydia thought, "What if that was me? I would want someone to help!" So Lydia went over and asked, "Can I help you?"

The person smiled big and said, "Yes, please! That's so kind of you!" Lydia helped as best as she could.

When it was done, the person said, "Thank you so much! You are a wonderful helper!" Lydia felt so happy inside, happier than when playing alone.

Her mom said, "I'm so proud of you for helping!" Lydia learned that helping others makes everyone feel good, especially yourself.



Once upon a time, a stubborn little boy named Eli went to the playground with his mommy. Eli loved to explore and discover new things.

While walking, Eli saw a deep pond. It looked exciting! He forgot what his mommy said about staying close. Eli ran toward it to take a closer look.

"Stop!" yelled his mommy. But Eli got too close and almost fell in! His mommy grabbed him just in time.

Eli's heart was beating fast. He was very scared. "Mommy, I'm sorry," Eli said with tears in his eyes.

His mommy hugged Eli tight. "I'm glad you're safe. Some places are dangerous, and that's why we must be careful." Eli promised to always listen and never wander off again.



Once upon a time, a little boy named Alfie went to the mall with his daddy. They were having a nice day together.

While his daddy was looking at something, a stranger came up to Alfie. The stranger smiled and said, "Would you like some candy? Come with me!"

Alfie remembered what his daddy had taught him. He said loudly, "No! I don't talk to strangers!" Then Alfie ran back to his daddy.

Alfie told his daddy what happened. Daddy was so proud! "You did the right thing! Never go anywhere with someone you don't know."

Alfie felt brave and safe. He learned that it's always okay to say no to strangers and run to a grown-up you trust.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Iris. One day, while playing in the hallway, Iris accidentally knocked over the family photo frame. It fell to the floor and broke!

Iris was very scared. When mommy came and asked what happened, Iris said, "I didn't do it! Maybe the wind did it!" But there was no wind inside the house.

Mommy looked at Iris with sad eyes. "Are you telling me the truth?" Iris looked at the floor and didn't say anything. She felt bad for lying.

Finally, Iris said, "I'm sorry, mommy. I did it. I was playing too rough and it was an accident. I was scared to tell you."

Mommy hugged Iris and said, "Thank you for telling the truth. Accidents happen, and I'm not angry. But lying makes things worse. Always tell the truth, even when you're scared." Iris felt much better after being honest.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Leo. Leo was always in a hurry. He never wanted to slow down!

One day, his mom said, "Be careful! Don't go so fast!" But Leo didn't listen. He was skating without looking, going faster and faster.

Suddenly, Leo tripped and fell! He scraped his knee and it hurt a lot. Leo started to cry.

His mom came and put a bandage on the scrape. "This is why I asked you to slow down," said mom gently.

Leo's knee hurt for several days. He learned that rushing can lead to accidents. It's better to slow down and be careful than to get hurt.



Once upon a time, there was a gentle little boy named Oscar. Oscar loved to play in the field. One day, his mom told him not to go near a sharp knife.

Oscar said, "Okay, mom!" But he was very curious. When mom wasn't looking, Oscar went close to a sharp knife. He thought it would be fun to explore.

But something bad happened. Oscar was grounded. He started to cry and called for his mom. Mom came running and helped him.

Oscar felt very sorry. He hugged his mom and said, "I'm sorry I didn't listen." Mom said, "I told you because I love you and want you to be safe."

From that day on, Oscar learned that he should always listen to his mom. Some rules are there to keep us safe.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Owen. One day, Owen saw a bottle on the counter. It looked like candy!

Owen reached for it, but his dad quickly took it away. "No! That's medicine, not candy!" said dad.

"But it looks yummy," said Owen. Dad sat down with Owen to explain something important.

"Medicine helps sick people feel better, but it can make healthy people very sick. Only grown-ups can give medicine, and only when someone needs it."

Owen understood now. Medicine is not a treat. He promised to never touch medicine bottles. Some things that look like candy can be dangerous!

But her daddy said, "Wait! We should only look, not touch. Some things in nature can be dangerous or need to stay where they are."

Daddy explained that touching the wrong things could hurt Flora or the animals. "We're just visitors here. We should respect nature."

Flora understood. She took pictures with her eyes instead of her hands. Looking is wonderful too! Flora learned to enjoy nature safely and respectfully.

Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Hugo. One day, Hugo heard some big kids say a word that sounded funny. So Hugo said it too!

Hugo didn't know! He just thought it sounded funny. But now he understood that some words can make people feel bad.

Hugo felt sorry for saying the bad word. He learned to think before speaking. Now Hugo uses kind words that make people smile!



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Alfie. After school, Alfie was supposed to do homework. But he wanted to play with toys instead!

"I'll do it later!" said Alfie, running off to play. His mom called, "Remember your homework!" But Alfie didn't listen.

Later came and went. Before Alfie knew it, it was bedtime! He hadn't done any homework. Now it was too late, and he was very tired.

The next day at school, the teacher was disappointed that Alfie didn't have his homework. Alfie felt embarrassed and sad.

After that, Alfie learned to do homework first, then play. When you finish your work first, you can play without worrying! Work first, then play—that's the best way!

Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Ivy. Ivy loved watching cartoons on the TV. She watched for hours and hours every day.

After many days of too much TV, Ivy's head started to hurt. Her eyes felt tired. She didn't feel good at all.

The doctor said Ivy needed to rest her eyes and play more. So Ivy went outside and discovered how fun it was to run and play!

Ivy learned that too much TV isn't good for you. Playing outside and using your imagination is much more fun. Now Ivy only watches a little TV each day.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Ethan. Ethan had a sister named Emma. One day, Emma got a new toy as a present.

Emma couldn't find her new thing and started to cry. Mom asked, "Ethan, do you know where it is?"

Ethan felt bad seeing Emma so sad. He went and got the new toy and said, "I'm sorry. I took it because I was jealous."

Mom explained, "Everyone gets different things at different times. Emma's special day will be your special day another time." Ethan hugged Emma and learned that jealousy only makes everyone sad.

Archie understood now. Fire is very serious. Only grown-ups can use things that make fire. He promised to never touch matches or lighters.

Once upon a time, a little girl named Daisy went to the park with her dad. They were having a nice day together.

While her dad was looking at something, a stranger came up to Daisy. The stranger smiled and said, "Would you like some candy? Come with me!"

Daisy remembered what her dad had taught her. She said loudly, "No! I don't talk to strangers!" Then Daisy ran back to her dad.

Daisy told her dad what happened. Dad was so proud! "You did the right thing! Never go anywhere with someone you don't know."

Daisy felt brave and safe. She learned that it's always okay to say no to strangers and run to a grown-up you trust.



Once upon a time, a little girl named Lily and a little girl named Nora were playing together. They both wanted to use the slide.

"Me first!" yelled Lily. "No, me first!" yelled Nora. They pushed and pulled, and soon they were both very upset.

An older kid saw them fighting and came over. "Why don't you take turns? One person goes, then the other person goes."

Lily went first for a little while, then it was Nora's turn. They kept switching, and guess what? They both got to play!

Lily and Nora learned that taking turns is fair. Everyone gets a chance, and no one feels left out. Now they always take turns and never fight!



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Archie who had a special building blocks. It was his favorite toy in the whole world!

But Archie didn't take good care of it. He left it outside in the rain, threw it around, and never put it away nicely.

One day, the building blocks broke! A piece fell off and it didn't work anymore. Archie was so sad and cried. He wanted his favorite toy back!

His mom said, "If you had taken better care of it, it might not have broken. Things need love and care."

Archie learned to take care of his things. He puts toys away nicely now and treats them gently. Taking care of our things makes them last longer!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Nina. For her birthday, Nina got clothes from her mommy.

But Nina wasn't happy. "This isn't what I wanted!" she complained. "I wanted something else!" Her mommy looked very sad.

Later, Nina saw a child who had no toys at all. That child looked at Nina's clothes and said, "Wow, you're so lucky!"

Nina suddenly felt bad for complaining. She realized that having any gift is special. Her mommy worked hard to give her something nice.

Nina ran to her mommy and said, "Thank you for my gift! I love it!" She learned to be grateful for what she has. Being thankful makes everyone happier!



Once upon a time, a gentle little girl named Violet went to the forest with her daddy. Violet loved to explore and discover new things.

While walking, Violet saw a steep cliff. It looked exciting! She forgot what her daddy said about staying close. Violet ran toward it to take a closer look.

"Stop!" yelled her daddy. But Violet got too close and almost fell in! Her daddy grabbed her just in time.

Violet's heart was beating fast. She was very scared. "Daddy, I'm sorry," Violet said with tears in her eyes.

Her daddy hugged Violet tight. "I'm glad you're safe. Some places are dangerous, and that's why we must be careful." Violet promised to always listen and never wander off again.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Luke who had a special doll. It was his favorite toy in the whole world!

But Luke didn't take good care of it. He left it outside in the rain, threw it around, and never put it away nicely.

One day, the doll broke! A piece fell off and it didn't work anymore. Luke was so sad and cried. He wanted his favorite toy back!

His mommy said, "If you had taken better care of it, it might not have broken. Things need love and care."

Luke learned to take care of his things. He puts toys away nicely now and treats them gently. Taking care of our things makes them last longer!



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Liam. Liam was standing on a chair, even though his mommy said not to.

While playing, Liam got a scrape! It hurt a lot and Liam started to cry. His mommy came running to help.

Mommy cleaned the boo-boo and gave Liam a bandage. "This is why I said to be careful," mommy explained gently.

Liam felt better after a hug and a kiss. But he learned an important lesson: the rules are there to keep him safe.

From then on, Liam remembered to be more careful. Getting hurt is no fun, and following the rules helps avoid accidents!



Once upon a time, a little boy named Ryan went to the lake with his grandpa. It was a hot day and the water looked so inviting!

His grandpa said, "Wait for me before going in the water." But Ryan was too excited. He ran and jumped right in!

The water was deeper than Ryan thought! He couldn't touch the bottom and got scared. He started to splash and cry for help.

His grandpa quickly jumped in and pulled Ryan out. They were both very shaken up.

Ryan learned an important lesson that day. Water can be dangerous! Always wait for a grown-up, and never swim alone. Now Ryan always asks for permission before going near water.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Zoe. Zoe had a favorite building blocks that she loved very much. She played with it every day.

One day, her little brother Leo came and asked, "Can I play with your building blocks?" But Zoe said, "No! It's mine! Go away!"

Leo was very sad and started to cry. Zoe kept playing alone, but it didn't feel fun anymore. She saw how sad Leo was and felt bad inside.

Finally, Zoe went to Leo and said, "I'm sorry. We can play together." Leo's face lit up with a big smile. They played with the building blocks together and had so much more fun!

Zoe learned that sharing makes everyone happy. When we share, we make more friends and have more fun.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Oscar. Oscar had a favorite toy car that he loved very much. He played with it every day.

One day, his little sister Ella came and asked, "Can I play with your toy car?" But Oscar said, "No! It's mine! Go away!"

Ella was very sad and started to cry. Oscar kept playing alone, but it didn't feel fun anymore. He saw how sad Ella was and felt bad inside.

Finally, Oscar went to Ella and said, "I'm sorry. We can play together." Ella's face lit up with a big smile. They played with the toy car together and had so much more fun!

Oscar learned that sharing makes everyone happy. When we share, we make more friends and have more fun.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Ella. Ella was always in a hurry. She never wanted to slow down!

One day, her dad said, "Be careful! Don't go so fast!" But Ella didn't listen. She was running by the pool, going faster and faster.

Suddenly, Ella tripped and fell! She scraped her knee and it hurt a lot. Ella started to cry.

Her dad came and put a bandage on the scrape. "This is why I asked you to slow down," said dad gently.

Ella's knee hurt for several days. She learned that rushing can lead to accidents. It's better to slow down and be careful than to get hurt.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Eli. Eli was always in a hurry. He never wanted to slow down!

One day, his daddy said, "Be careful! Don't go so fast!" But Eli didn't listen. He was skating without looking, going faster and faster.

Suddenly, Eli tripped and fell! He scraped his knee and it hurt a lot. Eli started to cry.

His daddy came and put a bandage on the scrape. "This is why I asked you to slow down," said daddy gently.

Eli's knee hurt for several days. He learned that rushing can lead to accidents. It's better to slow down and be careful than to get hurt.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Finn. Finn was jumping on furniture, even though his mommy said not to.

While playing, Finn got a scrape! It hurt a lot and Finn started to cry. His mommy came running to help.

Mommy cleaned the boo-boo and gave Finn a bandage. "This is why I said to be careful," mommy explained gently.

Finn felt better after a hug and a kiss. But he learned an important lesson: the rules are there to keep him safe.

From then on, Finn remembered to be more careful. Getting hurt is no fun, and following the rules helps avoid accidents!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Rose. Rose had a friend named Ethan. They promised to build a sandcastle the next day.

But when the next day came, Rose decided to do something else instead. She forgot all about the promise to Ethan.

Ethan waited and waited, but Rose never came. Ethan felt very sad and disappointed. When Rose saw Ethan later, Ethan was crying.

"You promised!" said Ethan. Rose suddenly remembered and felt terrible. "I'm so sorry," said Rose. "I forgot."

Rose learned that promises are very important. When we break a promise, we hurt our friends. From then on, Rose always kept her promises.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Owen. For his birthday, Owen got a book from his daddy.

But Owen wasn't happy. "This isn't what I wanted!" he complained. "I wanted something else!" His daddy looked very sad.

Later, Owen saw a child who had no toys at all. That child looked at Owen's book and said, "Wow, you're so lucky!"

Owen suddenly felt bad for complaining. He realized that having any gift is special. His daddy worked hard to give him something nice.

Owen ran to his daddy and said, "Thank you for my gift! I love it!" He learned to be grateful for what he has. Being thankful makes everyone happier!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Lily. Lily had a friend named Leah. They promised to play dress-up the next day.

But when the next day came, Lily decided to do something else instead. She forgot all about the promise to Leah.

Leah waited and waited, but Lily never came. Leah felt very sad and disappointed. When Lily saw Leah later, Leah was crying.

"You promised!" said Leah. Lily suddenly remembered and felt terrible. "I'm so sorry," said Lily. "I forgot."

Lily learned that promises are very important. When we break a promise, we hurt our friends. From then on, Lily always kept her promises.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Chloe. One day, Chloe saw matches on the table. They looked interesting!

Chloe reached for the matches, but her daddy quickly stopped her. "No! Those are very dangerous!" said daddy.

Daddy sat down with Chloe and explained. "Fire is not a toy. Matches and lighters can start fires that hurt people and burn things."

"If you ever see fire or smoke, you should tell a grown-up right away. And remember: Stop, Drop, and Roll if your clothes catch fire."

Chloe understood now. Fire is very serious. Only grown-ups can use things that make fire. She promised to never touch matches or lighters.



Once upon a time, there was a gentle little boy named Jake. Jake loved to play in the living room. One day, his daddy reminded him that matches was dangerous.

Jake said, "Okay, daddy!" But he was very curious. When daddy wasn't looking, Jake went close to matches. He thought it would be fun to explore.

But something bad happened. Jake got lost. He started to cry and called for his daddy. Daddy came running and helped him.

Jake felt very sorry. He hugged his daddy and said, "I'm sorry I didn't listen." Daddy said, "I told you because I love you and want you to be safe."

From that day on, Jake learned that he should always listen to his daddy. Some rules are there to keep us safe.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Violet who had a little hamster named Pepper. Violet loved Pepper very much.

One day, Violet was supposed to give Pepper food and water. But Violet was busy playing with toys and said, "I'll do it later!"

Later came and went, but Violet forgot all about Pepper. The little hamster got very hungry and thirsty. Pepper made sad little sounds.

Violet's dad said, "Did you feed Pepper?" Violet suddenly remembered and felt very bad. She ran to feed and give water to the hamster.

"Pepper depends on you," said her parent. "Pets need us to take care of them." Violet promised to always remember to care for Pepper first, because pets are family too.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Nina. One day, Nina saw mom with the dishes. At first, Nina just wanted to keep playing.

But then Nina thought, "What if that was me? I would want someone to help!" So Nina went over and asked, "Can I help you?"

The person smiled big and said, "Yes, please! That's so kind of you!" Nina helped as best as she could.

When it was done, the person said, "Thank you so much! You are a wonderful helper!" Nina felt so happy inside, happier than when playing alone.

Her mom said, "I'm so proud of you for helping!" Nina learned that helping others makes everyone feel good, especially yourself.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Max. Max had a sister named Rose. One day, Rose got a pretty dress as a present.

Max felt jealous. "Why did Rose get something and I didn't?" he thought. Max got so angry that he took the pretty dress and hid it!

Rose couldn't find her new thing and started to cry. Mommy asked, "Max, do you know where it is?"

Max felt bad seeing Rose so sad. He went and got the pretty dress and said, "I'm sorry. I took it because I was jealous."

Mommy explained, "Everyone gets different things at different times. Rose's special day will be your special day another time." Max hugged Rose and learned that jealousy only makes everyone sad.



Once upon a time, a little girl named Clara went to the hiking trail with her daddy. Clara loved exploring and seeing all the plants and animals.

While walking, Clara saw a wild animal. It looked so cool! Clara wanted to touch it and take it home.

But her daddy said, "Wait! We should only look, not touch. Some things in nature can be dangerous or need to stay where they are."

Daddy explained that touching the wrong things could hurt Clara or the animals. "We're just visitors here. We should respect nature."

Clara understood. She took pictures with her eyes instead of her hands. Looking is wonderful too! Clara learned to enjoy nature safely and respectfully.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Ava. Ava had a favorite doll that she loved very much. She played with it every day.

One day, her little brother Oscar came and asked, "Can I play with your doll?" But Ava said, "No! It's mine! Go away!"

Oscar was very sad and started to cry. Ava kept playing alone, but it didn't feel fun anymore. She saw how sad Oscar was and felt bad inside.

Finally, Ava went to Oscar and said, "I'm sorry. We can play together." Oscar's face lit up with a big smile. They played with the doll together and had so much more fun!

Ava learned that sharing makes everyone happy. When we share, we make more friends and have more fun.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Jake. At school, a bigger kid named Liam was mean to him. Liam called Jake names and made him feel sad.

Jake didn't want to go to school anymore. He would cry and feel scared. But he didn't tell anyone what was happening.

Finally, his mom noticed something was wrong. Jake told them about Liam. Together, they talked to the teacher.

The teacher helped stop the bullying. Liam learned that being mean is wrong. Jake learned that it's important to tell grown-ups when someone is being mean.

Jake felt safe again! He learned that telling someone isn't tattling—it's asking for help. We should always speak up when something is wrong!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Bella. One day, Bella heard some big kids say a word that sounded funny. So Bella said it too!

Her mom's face looked very surprised and sad. "Where did you learn that word?" asked mom. "That's a bad word that hurts people's feelings."

Bella didn't know! She just thought it sounded funny. But now she understood that some words can make people feel bad.

Mom explained, "Kind words make people happy. Mean words make people sad. We always want to use kind words."

Bella felt sorry for saying the bad word. She learned to think before speaking. Now Bella uses kind words that make people smile!



Once upon a time, a little boy named Drew went to the beach with his grandpa. Drew loved exploring and seeing all the plants and animals.

While walking, Drew saw a bird's nest. It looked so cool! Drew wanted to touch it and take it home.

But his grandpa said, "Wait! We should only look, not touch. Some things in nature can be dangerous or need to stay where they are."

Grandpa explained that touching the wrong things could hurt Drew or the animals. "We're just visitors here. We should respect nature."

Drew understood. He took pictures with his eyes instead of his hands. Looking is wonderful too! Drew learned to enjoy nature safely and respectfully.



Once upon a time, there was a helpful little boy named Henry. Henry loved to play in the garden. One day, his daddy said he should never touch a dark cave.

Henry said, "Okay, daddy!" But he was very curious. When daddy wasn't looking, Henry went close to a dark cave. He thought it would be fun to explore.

But something bad happened. Henry broke something precious. He started to cry and called for his daddy. Daddy came running and helped him.

Henry felt very sorry. He hugged his daddy and said, "I'm sorry I didn't listen." Daddy said, "I told you because I love you and want you to be safe."

From that day on, Henry learned that he should always listen to his daddy. Some rules are there to keep us safe.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Ryan. Every morning, Ryan didn't want to get up. He played and dawdled instead of getting ready.

One day, because Ryan was so slow, he missed the school bus! His dad had to drive him, and they were both late.

At school, Ryan had missed story time, the best part of the day! He was so sad. His friends had all the fun without him.

That night, his dad helped make a list: wake up, brush teeth, get dressed, eat breakfast. Ryan put stickers on the list when he finished each thing.

The next day, Ryan got ready quickly! He caught the bus and didn't miss anything. Having a routine makes mornings easier and better!



Once upon a time, a little boy named Liam went to the lake with his dad. It was a hot day and the water looked so inviting!

His dad said, "Wait for me before going in the water." But Liam was too excited. He ran and jumped right in!

The water was deeper than Liam thought! He couldn't touch the bottom and got scared. He started to splash and cry for help.

His dad quickly jumped in and pulled Liam out. They were both very shaken up.

Liam learned an important lesson that day. Water can be dangerous! Always wait for a grown-up, and never swim alone. Now Liam always asks for permission before going near water.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Alfie. One day, Alfie really wanted to skip bath time. But his mommy said no.

Alfie got very angry! He started to scream and cry and kick his feet. He threw a big tantrum right there!

But the tantrum didn't work. his mommy waited until Alfie calmed down. "Screaming won't change my answer," said mommy.

Alfie was tired from all the crying. He felt silly. The tantrum didn't get him what he wanted. It just made him tired and sad.

Alfie learned that throwing tantrums doesn't help. It's better to use words and accept when the answer is no. Sometimes grown-ups know what's best.

Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Owen. Owen only wanted to eat cake. "I don't like vegetables!" he would say every day.

His mommy tried to give Owen healthy food, but Owen always said no. He only ate cake for days and days.

Soon, Owen didn't feel good. His tummy hurt and he had no energy to play. The doctor said Owen needed to eat healthy food to feel better.

Owen tried the vegetables, just a tiny bite. Hey, it wasn't so bad! Actually, it was pretty good! He tried more healthy foods and started feeling much better.

Now Owen eats lots of good food that makes him strong. He still has treats sometimes, but he knows healthy food is important!

Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Bella. Bella never wanted to go to bed. "I'm not tired!" she always said.

One night, Bella stayed up very, very late playing with toys. Her daddy said, "Time for bed!" But Bella hid under the covers and kept playing.

The next day, Bella was so tired! She couldn't run. She couldn't play. She fell asleep at breakfast!

Her daddy said, "This is why we need sleep. Our bodies need rest to play and have fun."

That night, Bella went to bed on time. The next day, she had so much energy! Bella learned that sleep helps us feel good and have fun. Now bedtime isn't so bad!

Daddy heard the noise and came in. "Stop!" said daddy. "Fighting is not okay!" Both Theo and Violet were in trouble.

Theo and Violet said sorry to each other. They learned to take turns and talk instead of fight. Using words is much better than fighting!

Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Ava. Ava was afraid of the doctor. Whenever she saw the doctor, she would hide!

One day, her mommy said, "Let's try to be brave together." Ava was nervous but held her mommy's hand tight.

They faced the doctor slowly and carefully. At first, Ava was still scared. But her mommy was right there.

Little by little, Ava felt less afraid. She realized that with help, the doctor wasn't so scary after all!

Ava was so proud of being brave! She learned that it's okay to be afraid, but facing your fears makes you stronger. And having someone to help makes it easier.

Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Maya. One day, Maya took their snack to her friend Adam. Adam was very sad.

At first, Maya didn't want to say sorry. She felt embarrassed and a little stubborn. But Adam wouldn't play with her anymore.

Maya's dad said, "When we hurt someone, we need to say sorry. It helps fix the hurt."

Maya found Adam and said, "I'm really sorry for what I did. It was wrong. Can you forgive me?" Adam smiled and said yes.

They hugged and played together again! Maya learned that saying sorry is hard but important. It makes friendships strong and helps everyone feel better.

Once upon a time, a little girl named Ella wanted to carry heavy boxes. She tried and tried, but it was too hard to do alone!

Then Ella's friend Sam came by. "Need help?" asked Sam. At first, Ella said, "No, I can do it myself!"

But after trying more and failing, Ella finally said, "Okay, please help me." Together, they started working.

With two people helping, the job became easy! They finished quickly and had so much fun doing it together. They high-fived and celebrated!

Ella learned that it's okay to ask for help. Working together makes hard things easier and more fun. Two friends are better than one!

Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Ben. Ben had a favorite blocks that he loved very much. He played with it every day.

One day, his little sister Olive came and asked, "Can I play with your blocks?" But Ben said, "No! It's mine! Go away!"

Olive was very sad and started to cry. Ben kept playing alone, but it didn't feel fun anymore. He saw how sad Olive was and felt bad inside.

Finally, Ben went to Olive and said, "I'm sorry. We can play together." Olive's face lit up with a big smile. They played with the blocks together and had so much more fun!

Ben learned that sharing makes everyone happy. When we share, we make more friends and have more fun.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Theo. Theo was very excited about to open presents. But his mommy said he had to wait.

"I don't want to wait! I want it now!" said Theo. He started to stomp his feet and whine.

But being impatient didn't help. It just made Theo feel worse. his mommy said, "Being upset won't make time go faster."

Theo tried to be patient. He played with toys and helped his mommy. Before Theo knew it, it was time!

"Waiting wasn't so bad!" said Theo with a big smile. He learned that being patient and finding fun things to do makes waiting easier. Good things come to those who wait!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Sophie who had a brother named Sam. One day, they both wanted a toy.

"It's mine!" yelled Sophie. "No, it's mine!" yelled Sam. They started pushing and grabbing. Soon they were really fighting!

Daddy heard the noise and came in. "Stop!" said daddy. "Fighting is not okay!" Both Sophie and Sam were in trouble.

They had to sit in time-out and think about what they did. Daddy said, "Use your words, not your hands. Talk about problems."

Sophie and Sam said sorry to each other. They learned to take turns and talk instead of fight. Using words is much better than fighting!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Lily. One day, Lily really wanted a toy at the store. But her mommy said no.

Lily got very angry! She started to scream and cry and kick her feet. She threw a big tantrum right there!

But the tantrum didn't work. her mommy waited until Lily calmed down. "Screaming won't change my answer," said mommy.

Lily was tired from all the crying. She felt silly. The tantrum didn't get her what she wanted. It just made her tired and sad.

Lily learned that throwing tantrums doesn't help. It's better to use words and accept when the answer is no. Sometimes grown-ups know what's best.

Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Hugo. One day, Hugo heard some big kids say a word that sounded funny. So Hugo said it too!

His mom's face looked very surprised and sad. "Where did you learn that word?" asked mom. "That's a bad word that hurts people's feelings."

Hugo didn't know! He just thought it sounded funny. But now he understood that some words can make people feel bad.

Mom explained, "Kind words make people happy. Mean words make people sad. We always want to use kind words."

Hugo felt sorry for saying the bad word. He learned to think before speaking. Now Hugo uses kind words that make people smile!



Once upon a time, a little girl named Mia loved going to the playground. Her favorite thing was the swing.

One day, Mia wanted to show off. She climbed higher than she should and hung upside down in a silly way. "Look at me!" she yelled.

But then Mia lost her grip and fell! She hurt her arm and started to cry. Her dad came running.

At the doctor, they said Mia's arm would be okay, but she had to wear a bandage and rest. Mia couldn't play for a whole week!

Mia learned that playground rules are there to keep us safe. Showing off and being silly on equipment can lead to getting hurt. Play safe, have fun!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Daisy. One day, Daisy saw matches on the table. They looked interesting!

Daisy reached for the matches, but her mommy quickly stopped her. "No! Those are very dangerous!" said mommy.

Mommy sat down with Daisy and explained. "Fire is not a toy. Matches and lighters can start fires that hurt people and burn things."

"If you ever see fire or smoke, you should tell a grown-up right away. And remember: Stop, Drop, and Roll if your clothes catch fire."

Daisy understood now. Fire is very serious. Only grown-ups can use things that make fire. She promised to never touch matches or lighters.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Mia. One day, while playing in the bedroom, Mia accidentally knocked over mom's pretty bowl. It fell to the floor and broke!

Mia was very scared. When mom came and asked what happened, Mia said, "I didn't do it! Maybe the wind did it!" But there was no wind inside the house.

Mom looked at Mia with sad eyes. "Are you telling me the truth?" Mia looked at the floor and didn't say anything. She felt bad for lying.

Finally, Mia said, "I'm sorry, mom. I did it. I was playing too rough and it was an accident. I was scared to tell you."

Mom hugged Mia and said, "Thank you for telling the truth. Accidents happen, and I'm not angry. But lying makes things worse. Always tell the truth, even when you're scared." Mia felt much better after being honest.



Once upon a time, there was a caring little girl named Flora. Flora loved to play in the backyard. One day, her mommy said she should never touch deep water.

Flora said, "Okay, mommy!" But she was very curious. When mommy wasn't looking, Flora went close to deep water. She thought it would be fun to explore.

But something bad happened. Flora fell and got hurt. She started to cry and called for her mommy. Mommy came running and helped her.

Flora felt very sorry. She hugged her mommy and said, "I'm sorry I didn't listen." Mommy said, "I told you because I love you and want you to be safe."

From that day on, Flora learned that she should always listen to her mommy. Some rules are there to keep us safe.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Max. Max had a sister named Rose. One day, Rose got a shiny bike as a present.

Max felt jealous. "Why did Rose get something and I didn't?" he thought. Max got so angry that he took the shiny bike and hid it!

Rose couldn't find her new thing and started to cry. Dad asked, "Max, do you know where it is?"

Max felt bad seeing Rose so sad. He went and got the shiny bike and said, "I'm sorry. I took it because I was jealous."

Dad explained, "Everyone gets different things at different times. Rose's special day will be your special day another time." Max hugged Rose and learned that jealousy only makes everyone sad.

Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Stella. Stella never liked to clean up. Her room was always very messy!

One day, Stella couldn't find her pet hamster. She looked everywhere but there was so much stuff on the floor! Stella started to cry.

Her dad said, "If you kept your room clean, you could find your things." Stella knew dad was right.

Together, they cleaned the whole room. They picked up toys, folded clothes, and put things in their place. And guess what? They found the pet hamster!

Stella was so happy! She learned that keeping things clean helps you find what you need. A tidy room is a happy room!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Nora. Nora was standing on a chair, even though her daddy said not to.

Daddy cleaned the boo-boo and gave Nora a bandage. "This is why I said to be careful," daddy explained gently.

Nora felt better after a hug and a kiss. But she learned an important lesson: the rules are there to keep her safe.

From then on, Nora remembered to be more careful. Getting hurt is no fun, and following the rules helps avoid accidents!

Violet saw something shiny and colorful. Without thinking, she walked toward it, leaving her grandma behind. Violet walked and walked until...

She looked around and didn't see her grandma anywhere! Violet was lost! She felt very scared and started to cry.

A kind worker found Violet and helped find her grandma. When they were together again, Violet hugged her grandma so tight!

"Never wander off without me," said grandma. Violet learned to always stay close to her grandma in busy places. It's scary to be lost.

Ruby's knee hurt for several days. She learned that rushing can lead to accidents. It's better to slow down and be careful than to get hurt.

Finn learned that too much TV isn't good for you. Playing outside and using your imagination is much more fun. Now Finn only watches a little TV each day.

Mom explained that touching the wrong things could hurt Emma or the animals. "We're just visitors here. We should respect nature."

Emma understood. She took pictures with her eyes instead of her hands. Looking is wonderful too! Emma learned to enjoy nature safely and respectfully.

Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Adam. At school, a bigger kid named Cole was mean to him. Cole called Adam names and made him feel sad.

From then on, Henry remembered to be more careful. Getting hurt is no fun, and following the rules helps avoid accidents!



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Jack. One day, Jack saw a friend who lost a toy. At first, Jack just wanted to keep playing.

But then Jack thought, "What if that was me? I would want someone to help!" So Jack went over and asked, "Can I help you?"

The person smiled big and said, "Yes, please! That's so kind of you!" Jack helped as best as he could.

When it was done, the person said, "Thank you so much! You are a wonderful helper!" Jack felt so happy inside, happier than when playing alone.

His dad said, "I'm so proud of you for helping!" Jack learned that helping others makes everyone feel good, especially yourself.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Tommy who had a sister named Iris. One day, they both wanted whose turn it was.

"It's mine!" yelled Tommy. "No, it's mine!" yelled Iris. They started pushing and grabbing. Soon they were really fighting!

Dad heard the noise and came in. "Stop!" said dad. "Fighting is not okay!" Both Tommy and Iris were in trouble.

They had to sit in time-out and think about what they did. Dad said, "Use your words, not your hands. Talk about problems."

Tommy and Iris said sorry to each other. They learned to take turns and talk instead of fight. Using words is much better than fighting!



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Drew. Drew never liked to clean up. His room was always very messy!

One day, Drew couldn't find his best book. He looked everywhere but there was so much stuff on the floor! Drew started to cry.

His mommy said, "If you kept your room clean, you could find your things." Drew knew mommy was right.

Together, they cleaned the whole room. They picked up toys, folded clothes, and put things in their place. And guess what? They found the best book!

Drew was so happy! He learned that keeping things clean helps you find what you need. A tidy room is a happy room!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Nora. Nora didn't like to listen to rules. She thought rules were boring!

One day, Nora's daddy said not to do something. But Nora didn't listen. She kept running away from parents at the store anyway.

Then something bad happened. Nora got lost for a very long time. She wished she had listened!

Nora's daddy wasn't angry, just sad. "I told you because I love you and want to keep you safe," daddy said.

Nora finally understood. Rules aren't to be mean—they're to protect us! She learned that lesson the hard way. Now she listens more carefully.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Ava. Ava never liked to clean up. Her room was always very messy!

Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Zach. At school, a bigger kid named Tommy was mean to him. Tommy called Zach names and made him feel sad.

Zach didn't want to go to school anymore. He would cry and feel scared. But he didn't tell anyone what was happening.

Finally, his mom noticed something was wrong. Zach told them about Tommy. Together, they talked to the teacher.

The teacher helped stop the bullying. Tommy learned that being mean is wrong. Zach learned that it's important to tell grown-ups when someone is being mean.

Zach felt safe again! He learned that telling someone isn't tattling—it's asking for help. We should always speak up when something is wrong!



Once upon a time, a little girl named Emma went to the park with her dad. Emma loved exploring and seeing all the plants and animals.

While walking, Emma saw a bee hive. It looked so cool! Emma wanted to touch it and take it home.

But her dad said, "Wait! We should only look, not touch. Some things in nature can be dangerous or need to stay where they are."

Dad explained that touching the wrong things could hurt Emma or the animals. "We're just visitors here. We should respect nature."

Emma understood. She took pictures with her eyes instead of her hands. Looking is wonderful too! Emma learned to enjoy nature safely and respectfully.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Charlie. One day at the park, Charlie saw a new little girl named Ivy.

At first, Charlie was too shy to say hello. What if the new kid didn't like him? Charlie just watched from far away.

But then Charlie thought, "Maybe Ivy wants a friend too!" So Charlie walked over and said, "Hi! Want to play?"

Ivy's face lit up with a big smile. "Yes! I was hoping someone would ask!" They played together and had so much fun!

Charlie learned that being brave and saying hello can make new friends. Everyone wants to be included. Now Charlie and Ivy are best friends!

Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Alfie. One day, Alfie heard some big kids say a word that sounded funny. So Alfie said it too!

His mom's face looked very surprised and sad. "Where did you learn that word?" asked mom. "That's a bad word that hurts people's feelings."

Alfie didn't know! He just thought it sounded funny. But now he understood that some words can make people feel bad.

Mom explained, "Kind words make people happy. Mean words make people sad. We always want to use kind words."

Alfie felt sorry for saying the bad word. He learned to think before speaking. Now Alfie uses kind words that make people smile!

Once upon a time, a little boy named Felix went to the lake with his grandma. It was a hot day and the water looked so inviting!

His grandma said, "Wait for me before going in the water." But Felix was too excited. He ran and jumped right in!

The water was deeper than Felix thought! He couldn't touch the bottom and got scared. He started to splash and cry for help.

His grandma quickly jumped in and pulled Felix out. They were both very shaken up.

Felix learned an important lesson that day. Water can be dangerous! Always wait for a grown-up, and never swim alone. Now Felix always asks for permission before going near water.

Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Henry. Henry was afraid of the doctor. Whenever he saw the doctor, he would hide!

One day, his dad said, "Let's try to be brave together." Henry was nervous but held his dad's hand tight.

They faced the doctor slowly and carefully. At first, Henry was still scared. But his dad was right there.

Little by little, Henry felt less afraid. He realized that with help, the doctor wasn't so scary after all!

Henry was so proud of being brave! He learned that it's okay to be afraid, but facing your fears makes you stronger. And having someone to help makes it easier.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Ryan. Ryan only wanted to eat cake. "I don't like broccoli!" he would say every day.

His mommy tried to give Ryan healthy food, but Ryan always said no. He only ate cake for days and days.

Soon, Ryan didn't feel good. His tummy hurt and he had no energy to play. The doctor said Ryan needed to eat healthy food to feel better.

Ryan tried the broccoli, just a tiny bite. Hey, it wasn't so bad! Actually, it was pretty good! He tried more healthy foods and started feeling much better.

Now Ryan eats lots of good food that makes him strong. He still has treats sometimes, but he knows healthy food is important!

Rose couldn't find her new thing and started to cry. Mom asked, "Hugo, do you know where it is?"

Iris learned that playground rules are there to keep us safe. Showing off and being silly on equipment can lead to getting hurt. Play safe, have fun!



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Sam. One day, while playing in the house, Sam accidentally knocked over grandma's old clock. It fell to the floor and broke!

Sam was very scared. When mommy came and asked what happened, Sam said, "I didn't do it! Maybe the wind did it!" But there was no wind inside the house.

Mommy looked at Sam with sad eyes. "Are you telling me the truth?" Sam looked at the floor and didn't say anything. He felt bad for lying.

Finally, Sam said, "I'm sorry, mommy. I did it. I was playing too rough and it was an accident. I was scared to tell you."

Mommy hugged Sam and said, "Thank you for telling the truth. Accidents happen, and I'm not angry. But lying makes things worse. Always tell the truth, even when you're scared." Sam felt much better after being honest.

Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Flora. One day, Flora saw matches on the table. They looked interesting!

Flora reached for the matches, but her mommy quickly stopped her. "No! Those are very dangerous!" said mommy.

Mommy sat down with Flora and explained. "Fire is not a toy. Matches and lighters can start fires that hurt people and burn things."

"If you ever see fire or smoke, you should tell a grown-up right away. And remember: Stop, Drop, and Roll if your clothes catch fire."

Flora understood now. Fire is very serious. Only grown-ups can use things that make fire. She promised to never touch matches or lighters.

The person smiled big and said, "Yes, please! That's so kind of you!" Adam helped as best as he could.

When it was done, the person said, "Thank you so much! You are a wonderful helper!" Adam felt so happy inside, happier than when playing alone.

His mom said, "I'm so proud of you for helping!" Adam learned that helping others makes everyone feel good, especially yourself.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Zoe who had a little puppy named Fluffy. Zoe loved Fluffy very much.

One day, Zoe was supposed to give Fluffy food and water. But Zoe was busy playing with toys and said, "I'll do it later!"

Later came and went, but Zoe forgot all about Fluffy. The little puppy got very hungry and thirsty. Fluffy made sad little sounds.

Zoe's mom said, "Did you feed Fluffy?" Zoe suddenly remembered and felt very bad. She ran to feed and give water to the puppy.

"Fluffy depends on you," said her parent. "Pets need us to take care of them." Zoe promised to always remember to care for Fluffy first, because pets are family too.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Nina. One day, Nina called them a name to her friend Tommy. Tommy was very sad.

At first, Nina didn't want to say sorry. She felt embarrassed and a little stubborn. But Tommy wouldn't play with her anymore.

Nina's mom said, "When we hurt someone, we need to say sorry. It helps fix the hurt."

Nina found Tommy and said, "I'm really sorry for what I did. It was wrong. Can you forgive me?" Tommy smiled and said yes.

They hugged and played together again! Nina learned that saying sorry is hard but important. It makes friendships strong and helps everyone feel better.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Olive. Olive had a brother named Ethan. One day, Ethan got a new toy as a present.

Olive felt jealous. "Why did Ethan get something and I didn't?" she thought. Olive got so angry that she took the new toy and hid it!

Ethan couldn't find his new thing and started to cry. Daddy asked, "Olive, do you know where it is?"

Olive felt bad seeing Ethan so sad. She went and got the new toy and said, "I'm sorry. I took it because I was jealous."

Daddy explained, "Everyone gets different things at different times. Ethan's special day will be your special day another time." Olive hugged Ethan and learned that jealousy only makes everyone sad.



Once upon a time, a helpful little girl named Luna went to the beach with her grandpa. Luna loved to explore and discover new things.

While walking, Luna saw an old well. It looked exciting! She forgot what her grandpa said about staying close. Luna ran toward it to take a closer look.

"Stop!" yelled her grandpa. But Luna got too close and almost fell in! Her grandpa grabbed her just in time.

Luna's heart was beating fast. She was very scared. "Grandpa, I'm sorry," Luna said with tears in her eyes.

Her grandpa hugged Luna tight. "I'm glad you're safe. Some places are dangerous, and that's why we must be careful." Luna promised to always listen and never wander off again.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Ethan who had a special kite. It was his favorite toy in the whole world!

But Ethan didn't take good care of it. He left it outside in the rain, threw it around, and never put it away nicely.

One day, the kite broke! A piece fell off and it didn't work anymore. Ethan was so sad and cried. He wanted his favorite toy back!

His daddy said, "If you had taken better care of it, it might not have broken. Things need love and care."

Ethan learned to take care of his things. He puts toys away nicely now and treats them gently. Taking care of our things makes them last longer!



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Noah. One day, Noah saw matches on the table. They looked interesting!

Noah reached for the matches, but his dad quickly stopped him. "No! Those are very dangerous!" said dad.

Dad sat down with Noah and explained. "Fire is not a toy. Matches and lighters can start fires that hurt people and burn things."

"If you ever see fire or smoke, you should tell a grown-up right away. And remember: Stop, Drop, and Roll if your clothes catch fire."

Noah understood now. Fire is very serious. Only grown-ups can use things that make fire. He promised to never touch matches or lighters.



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Liam. One day, his mom made delicious fruit for Liam and his little sister Ella.

Mom put the fruit on the table. "Make sure you share nicely," said mom. But Liam wanted all the fruit for himself!

When Ella wasn't looking, Liam took most of the fruit. He ate and ate until his tummy hurt very much!

Liam felt sick and couldn't play anymore. Ella was sad because there wasn't enough fruit left. Mom came and saw what happened.

"Being greedy doesn't make you happy," said mom. "Now you don't feel good, and Ella is sad." Liam said sorry to Ella and learned that being greedy only makes everyone feel bad.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Ella. One day at the playground, Ella saw a new little boy named Liam.

At first, Ella was too shy to say hello. What if the new kid didn't like her? Ella just watched from far away.

But then Ella thought, "Maybe Liam wants a friend too!" So Ella walked over and said, "Hi! Want to play?"

Liam's face lit up with a big smile. "Yes! I was hoping someone would ask!" They played together and had so much fun!

Ella learned that being brave and saying hello can make new friends. Everyone wants to be included. Now Ella and Liam are best friends!



Once upon a time, a little boy named Cole and a little boy named Max were playing together. They both wanted to use the swing.

"Me first!" yelled Cole. "No, me first!" yelled Max. They pushed and pulled, and soon they were both very upset.

An older kid saw them fighting and came over. "Why don't you take turns? One person goes, then the other person goes."

Cole went first for a little while, then it was Max's turn. They kept switching, and guess what? They both got to play!

Cole and Max learned that taking turns is fair. Everyone gets a chance, and no one feels left out. Now they always take turns and never fight!



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Tim. One day, while playing in the playroom, Tim accidentally knocked over grandma's old clock. It fell to the floor and broke!

Tim was very scared. When mom came and asked what happened, Tim said, "I didn't do it! Maybe the wind did it!" But there was no wind inside the house.

Mom looked at Tim with sad eyes. "Are you telling me the truth?" Tim looked at the floor and didn't say anything. He felt bad for lying.

Finally, Tim said, "I'm sorry, mom. I did it. I was playing too rough and it was an accident. I was scared to tell you."

Mom hugged Tim and said, "Thank you for telling the truth. Accidents happen, and I'm not angry. But lying makes things worse. Always tell the truth, even when you're scared." Tim felt much better after being honest.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Olive. Olive never liked to clean up. Her room was always very messy!

One day, Olive couldn't find her best book. She looked everywhere but there was so much stuff on the floor! Olive started to cry.

Her mommy said, "If you kept your room clean, you could find your things." Olive knew mommy was right.

Together, they cleaned the whole room. They picked up toys, folded clothes, and put things in their place. And guess what? They found the best book!

Olive was so happy! She learned that keeping things clean helps you find what you need. A tidy room is a happy room!



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Ben. Ben was afraid of the doctor. Whenever he saw the doctor, he would hide!

One day, his daddy said, "Let's try to be brave together." Ben was nervous but held his daddy's hand tight.

They faced the doctor slowly and carefully. At first, Ben was still scared. But his daddy was right there.

Little by little, Ben felt less afraid. He realized that with help, the doctor wasn't so scary after all!

Ben was so proud of being brave! He learned that it's okay to be afraid, but facing your fears makes you stronger. And having someone to help makes it easier.

Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Milo. Milo never wanted to go to bed. "I'm not tired!" he always said.

One night, Milo stayed up very, very late playing with toys. His mom said, "Time for bed!" But Milo hid under the covers and kept playing.

The next day, Milo was so tired! He couldn't run. He couldn't play. He fell asleep at breakfast!

His mom said, "This is why we need sleep. Our bodies need rest to play and have fun."

That night, Milo went to bed on time. The next day, he had so much energy! Milo learned that sleep helps us feel good and have fun. Now bedtime isn't so bad!

Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Nora. For her birthday, Nora got a toy from her mommy.

But Nora wasn't happy. "This isn't what I wanted!" she complained. "I wanted something else!" Her mommy looked very sad.

Later, Nora saw a child who had no toys at all. That child looked at Nora's toy and said, "Wow, you're so lucky!"

Nora suddenly felt bad for complaining. She realized that having any gift is special. Her mommy worked hard to give her something nice.

Nora ran to her mommy and said, "Thank you for my gift! I love it!" She learned to be grateful for what she has. Being thankful makes everyone happier!

Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Iris. Iris only wanted to eat soda. "I don't like fruits!" she would say every day.

Her mom tried to give Iris healthy food, but Iris always said no. She only ate soda for days and days.

Soon, Iris didn't feel good. Her tummy hurt and she had no energy to play. The doctor said Iris needed to eat healthy food to feel better.

Iris tried the fruits, just a tiny bite. Hey, it wasn't so bad! Actually, it was pretty good! She tried more healthy foods and started feeling much better.

Now Iris eats lots of good food that makes her strong. She still has treats sometimes, but she knows healthy food is important!



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Milo. For his birthday, Milo got a book from his daddy.

But Milo wasn't happy. "This isn't what I wanted!" he complained. "I wanted something else!" His daddy looked very sad.

Once upon a time, a little girl named Maya went to the beach with her daddy. It was a hot day and the water looked so inviting!

Her daddy said, "Wait for me before going in the water." But Maya was too excited. She ran and jumped right in!

The water was deeper than Maya thought! She couldn't touch the bottom and got scared. She started to splash and cry for help.

Her daddy quickly jumped in and pulled Maya out. They were both very shaken up.

Maya learned an important lesson that day. Water can be dangerous! Always wait for a grown-up, and never swim alone. Now Maya always asks for permission before going near water.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Stella. After school, Stella was supposed to do homework. But she wanted to play with toys instead!

"I'll do it later!" said Stella, running off to play. Her mommy called, "Remember your homework!" But Stella didn't listen.

Later came and went. Before Stella knew it, it was bedtime! She hadn't done any homework. Now it was too late, and she was very tired.

The next day at school, the teacher was disappointed that Stella didn't have her homework. Stella felt embarrassed and sad.

After that, Stella learned to do homework first, then play. When you finish your work first, you can play without worrying! Work first, then play—that's the best way!



Once upon a time, a little girl named Iris went to the park with her mommy. Iris loved exploring and seeing all the plants and animals.

While walking, Iris saw a bee hive. It looked so cool! Iris wanted to touch it and take it home.

But her mommy said, "Wait! We should only look, not touch. Some things in nature can be dangerous or need to stay where they are."

Mommy explained that touching the wrong things could hurt Iris or the animals. "We're just visitors here. We should respect nature."

Iris understood. She took pictures with her eyes instead of her hands. Looking is wonderful too! Iris learned to enjoy nature safely and respectfully.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Leah. Leah was always in a hurry. She never wanted to slow down!

One day, her dad said, "Be careful! Don't go so fast!" But Leah didn't listen. She was skating without looking, going faster and faster.

Suddenly, Leah tripped and fell! She scraped her knee and it hurt a lot. Leah started to cry.

Her dad came and put a bandage on the scrape. "This is why I asked you to slow down," said dad gently.

Leah's knee hurt for several days. She learned that rushing can lead to accidents. It's better to slow down and be careful than to get hurt.



Once upon a time, a little girl named Mia went to the park with her grandma. They were having a nice day together.

While her grandma was looking at something, a stranger came up to Mia. The stranger smiled and said, "Would you like some candy? Come with me!"

Mia remembered what her grandma had taught her. She said loudly, "No! I don't talk to strangers!" Then Mia ran back to her grandma.

Mia told her grandma what happened. Grandma was so proud! "You did the right thing! Never go anywhere with someone you don't know."

Mia felt brave and safe. She learned that it's always okay to say no to strangers and run to a grown-up you trust.



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Violet. One day, Violet heard some big kids say a word that sounded funny. So Violet said it too!

Her dad's face looked very surprised and sad. "Where did you learn that word?" asked dad. "That's a bad word that hurts people's feelings."

Violet didn't know! She just thought it sounded funny. But now she understood that some words can make people feel bad.

Dad explained, "Kind words make people happy. Mean words make people sad. We always want to use kind words."

Violet felt sorry for saying the bad word. She learned to think before speaking. Now Violet uses kind words that make people smile!

Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Lydia. Lydia had a favorite balloon that she loved very much. She played with it every day.

One day, her little brother Felix came and asked, "Can I play with your balloon?" But Lydia said, "No! It's mine! Go away!"

Felix was very sad and started to cry. Lydia kept playing alone, but it didn't feel fun anymore. She saw how sad Felix was and felt bad inside.

Finally, Lydia went to Felix and said, "I'm sorry. We can play together." Felix's face lit up with a big smile. They played with the balloon together and had so much more fun!

Lydia learned that sharing makes everyone happy. When we share, we make more friends and have more fun.



Once upon a time, a little girl named Ava went to the fair with her dad. There were so many exciting things to see!

Ava saw something shiny and colorful. Without thinking, she walked toward it, leaving her dad behind. Ava walked and walked until...

She looked around and didn't see her dad anywhere! Ava was lost! She felt very scared and started to cry.

A kind worker found Ava and helped find her dad. When they were together again, Ava hugged her dad so tight!

"Never wander off without me," said dad. Ava learned to always stay close to her dad in busy places. It's scary to be lost.

Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Cole. Every morning, Cole didn't want to get up. He played and dawdled instead of getting ready.

One day, because Cole was so slow, he missed the school bus! His mom had to drive him, and they were both late.

At school, Cole had missed story time, the best part of the day! He was so sad. His friends had all the fun without him.

That night, his mom helped make a list: wake up, brush teeth, get dressed, eat breakfast. Cole put stickers on the list when he finished each thing.

The next day, Cole got ready quickly! He caught the bus and didn't miss anything. Having a routine makes mornings easier and better!



Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Maya who had a brother named Felix. One day, they both wanted the TV remote.

"It's mine!" yelled Maya. "No, it's mine!" yelled Felix. They started pushing and grabbing. Soon they were really fighting!

Mom heard the noise and came in. "Stop!" said mom. "Fighting is not okay!" Both Maya and Felix were in trouble.

They had to sit in time-out and think about what they did. Mom said, "Use your words, not your hands. Talk about problems."

Maya and Felix said sorry to each other. They learned to take turns and talk instead of fight. Using words is much better than fighting!



Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Tim. Tim was jumping on furniture, even though his daddy said not to.

While playing, Tim hurt their finger! It hurt a lot and Tim started to cry. His daddy came running to help.

Daddy cleaned the boo-boo and gave Tim a bandage. "This is why I said to be careful," daddy explained gently.

Tim felt better after a hug and a kiss. But he learned an important lesson: the rules are there to keep him safe.

From then on, Tim remembered to be more careful. Getting hurt is no fun, and following the rules helps avoid accidents!



Once upon a time, a little boy named Charlie wanted to build a tall tower with blocks. He tried and tried, but it was too hard to do alone!

Then Charlie's friend Ben came by. "Need help?" asked Ben. At first, Charlie said, "No, I can do it myself!"

But after trying more and failing, Charlie finally said, "Okay, please help me." Together, they started working.

With two people helping, the job became easy! They finished quickly and had so much fun doing it together. They high-fived and celebrated!

Charlie learned that it's okay to ask for help. Working together makes hard things easier and more fun. Two friends are better than one!
